- **UX behavior:** Open-from-search (search-1): once WP04 posts `SessionBox(session, searchTerm: query)` from a result row, clicking a search result opens the transcript with the find bar already visible and prefilled with that query; after the ~200ms debounced scan the first match auto-scrolls to center and the bar reads \"1/N\". Zero matches in the loaded prefix → \"No matches\"; partially loaded transcript → the existing \"Search covers loaded messages only. / Load all\" hint appears (unchanged). When no query is supplied (popover double-click, command palette, parent/child navigation — every current SessionBox(session) caller), the bar stays closed and empty exactly as today.\n\nTyping in the find bar (transcript-3/-4): each keystroke resets currentMatchIndex to -1 and clears scrollTarget; after debounce, if there are matches the first is auto-selected (currentMatchIndex=0) and scrolled to center, bar shows \"1/N\". Editing the query restarts from the top rather than keeping a stale position. Empty query → matchIndices empty (early return), \"No matches\", no scroll.\n\nReturn (transcript-2): pressing Return in the find field advances to the next match (wraps N→1), identical to the down chevron / ⌘G. Shift-Return is unbound (⌘⇧G covers reverse).\n\nText mode (transcript-1): switching to Text view with an active query highlights every occurrence (yellow background) and Prev/Next/Return/auto-scroll move the matched row into view (rows now carry `.id(msg.id)`). Previously the bar showed a count but did nothing in Text mode.\n\nCurrent match (both modes): conveyed by the N/M counter in the find bar plus auto-scroll-of-the-active-match to center. No distinct accent color is added in either mode (the Session-mode color lives in ColorBarMessageView, not owned here; the Text-mode-only orange accent from the earlier draft is cut to avoid asymmetric treatment).\n\nJump-to-top (transcript-6): a small floating up-chevron appears bottom-trailing of the transcript when there is more than one message; tapping it animates a scroll to the first message. Hidden for single/empty transcripts.\n\nEdge cases: missing/empty transcript → find bar has nothing to scroll, scroll-to-top hidden, no crash (guards on displayIndexed.isEmpty/.first and `indices.first`). Partially loaded → search + auto-scroll operate over the loaded prefix with the existing disclosure banner. Session switch → existing reset (412-430) clears searchText/currentMatchIndex/scrollTarget; searchTerm priming only fires on the initial open of a session passed with a term, and MainWindowView clears pendingSearchTerm on screen-change so a stale term can't leak into the next session.
- **Acceptance:**
  - SessionBox exposes `searchTerm: String?` (default nil) and existing `SessionBox(session)` call sites compile unchanged; MainWindowView passes `pendingSearchTerm` into SessionDetailView and clears it on screen change.
  - SessionDetailView exposes `searchTerm: String?` and, when non-nil/non-empty, opens with showFind=true and searchText==searchTerm; when nil, showFind stays false and searchText stays empty (no behavior change for existing callers).
  - Typing a query that has matches auto-scrolls to and selects the first match (bar shows 1/N) without the user pressing Next; the empty-query path does not scroll (early return preserved).
  - Editing/clearing-and-retyping the query resets currentMatchIndex (via .onChange) so navigation restarts from the first match of the new result set; the auto-select is guarded by `currentMatchIndex < 0` so an in-progress Prev/Next is not yanked back by a re-scan.
  - Pressing Return in the find field advances to the next match (wrapping), matching the down-chevron / ⌘G behavior.
  - In Text view mode, an active query highlights matches AND Prev/Next/Return scroll the matched row into view (Text-mode rows carry `.id(msg.id)`).
  - A scroll-to-top control returns a deeply-scrolled long transcript to the first message via the existing ScrollViewReader proxy; hidden when ≤1 message.
  - All existing find behavior (Session-mode highlight, ⌘F toggle, ⌘G nav, partial-load hint, per-session reset, Copy paths) is unchanged.
- **Test plan:** Add macos/EngramTests/TranscriptFindTests.swift (XCTestCase, @testable import Engram; auto-included via the directory-based EngramTests target), following the established TranscriptLabelAndCopyTests #filePath source-assertion + pure-logic pattern (no ViewInspector in-target).\n\n1. Pure-logic (no view host) — exercises the real index math the new code depends on:\n - testAutoSelectsFirstMatchFromUnsetIndex: SessionDetailView.displayedFindMatchIndex(current: -1, count: 3) == 0; and nextFindMatchIndex advances 0→1→2→0 (wrap), locking the auto-select-first + wrap contract.\n - testResetIndexClampsToTop: for any non-empty count, displayedFindMatchIndex(current: -1, count: n) == 0, encoding transcript-4's restart-from-top.\n\n2. Source-contract assertions (read each owned file via #filePath; use normalized/looser substrings — strip whitespace or assert on `onSubmit`+`onNext` separately rather than the exact `.onSubmit { onNext() }` formatting, per the critique's brittleness note):\n - AppNotifications.swift: contains `searchTerm` on SessionBox.\n - MainWindowView.swift: contains `pendingSearchTerm` and a `searchTerm:` argument passed to SessionDetailView and a `box.searchTerm` read.\n - SessionDetailView.swift: contains `searchText = searchTerm` (priming, replacing the bare unconditional `searchText = \"\"` on the term path); contains `.onChange(of: searchText)` whose closure sets `currentMatchIndex = -1`; contains the auto-select assignment `currentMatchIndex = 0` guarded by `currentMatchIndex < 0` and positioned after `matchIndices = indices`; the `.text` ForEach contains `.id(msg.id)` and `RawMessageRow(` is called with `searchText:`.\n - TranscriptFindBar.swift: contains `onSubmit` and `onNext` (assert both substrings, not exact brace formatting).\n\nRationale: these are SwiftUI view-graph wirings not exercisable headlessly in this target; the existing suite uses identical #filePath assertions to lock view-wiring contracts. The pure-logic tests give real coverage of the index selection/clamp/wrap the new auto-select and reset rely on.
- **Risks:** searchTerm priming runs inside the per-session `.task(id: session.id)` reset; it replaces the single priming site at line 428 so no later stray `searchText = \"\"` can clobber it (verified exactly one priming site). Ordering: the auto-select block must sit AFTER `matchIndices = indices` (line 153) and the empty-query early return (line 143) must stay intact, or an empty query could auto-scroll against a stale matchIndices — the spec pins both. Interaction determinism: onChange sets currentMatchIndex=-1; the scan's `currentMatchIndex < 0` guard then sets 0 — sequence is deterministic, and the same guard prevents a filter/page re-scan (displayVersion bump → matchScanToken change → re-run) from yanking a user who already navigated (currentMatchIndex>=0) back to the first match. Text-mode `.id(msg.id)` relies on ChatMessage.id stability across the off-main rebuild; appended pages preserve instance identity (per the rebuildIndexed comment) and IndexedMessage.id mirrors ChatMessage.id, so the scrollTarget UUID resolves to a real Text anchor. Cross-WP dependency (the ONLY one): search-1's user-visible behavior fires only once WP04 swaps the SearchPageView result-row post from `SessionBox(session)` to `SessionBox(session, searchTerm: query)` — a single additive argument; until then WP03's carrier is wired and inert (every other caller passes nil), which is correct and non-regressing. Stale-term leak: mitigated by clearing pendingSearchTerm in the existing selectedScreen reset.
- **Out of scope:** This WP does NOT: (1) add a distinct current-match accent COLOR in either view mode. Session-mode color lives in ColorBarMessageView.swift (not owned here); the Text-mode-only orange accent from the earlier draft is intentionally CUT to avoid asymmetric current-match treatment for a Low finding. Current match is conveyed by the N/M counter + auto-scroll-to-center in both modes. session-detail-transcript-5 is therefore explicitly PARTIAL/DEFERRED — removed from findingsCovered; closing it for the default Session-mode path requires editing ColorBarMessageView.swift, owned by the WP that owns that file. (2) Preserve rich SegmentedMessageView rendering (markdown/code/copy-buttons) during an active search — session-detail-transcript-7's fallback lives in ColorBarMessageView.swift + ContentSegmentViews.swift, neither owned; removed from findingsCovered and DEFERRED to the owning WP. (3) Persist recent queries / search-history chips — search-4 has no persistence backend and this WP writes zero code for it; removed from findingsCovered and DEFERRED to WP04 (which owns SearchPageView's empty-state chip UI). (4) Bind Shift-Return → onPrev (SwiftUI .onSubmit has no modifier; ⌘⇧G already covers reverse). (5) Edit TranscriptToolbar (scroll-to-top is an overlay on the owned ScrollView region). Remaining cross-WP dependency for search-1: WP04 must change the SearchPageView result-row open from `SessionBox(session)` to `SessionBox(session, searchTerm: query)` — one additive argument — for the carrier WP03 built to fire.

### WP04 — Search page + palette: remove dead semantic/hybrid mode selector and embedding pill, distinguish search-failure from empty results, and fix the cutover scan test that guards the now-deleted controls

- **Disposition:** mixed  ·  **Critique:** needs-revision (revised)
- **Closes:** search-2, search-3, xc-states-4, command-palette-5
- **Goal:** Make the keyword-only Swift search honest and trustworthy: stop advertising semantic/hybrid search the product cannot run (the mode selector and the "N/M embedded" pill), and replace the false "No results" shown on a double-fault (service + local FTS both throw) with a distinct "Search unavailable" error state on both SearchPageView and CommandPaletteView. Because the existing cutover scan test asserts the presence of the very controls this WP deletes, that test is brought into scope and updated in the same change set so CI stays green.
- **Approach:** Three in-scope surgical changes plus a mandatory test-fix, each tracing to one finding. The cross-WP query-carry row from the original spec is DROPPED from this WP (see outOfScopeNotes) because it requires editing macos/Engram/AppNotifications.swift, which is owned by no work-package and is NOT in WP03's file list — so the dependency cannot be honestly stated as "WP03 owns it." It is re-scoped as a separate cross-cutting handoff.

(1) search-2 / remove-misleading — delete the unreachable mode selector. In SearchPageView.swift remove `@State selectedMode` (line 51), the `availableModes` computed property (lines 65-67), the `if availableModes.count > 1 { ForEach … }` mode-pill block (lines 141-158), and the two `if !availableModes.contains(selectedMode) { selectedMode = … }` re-selection blocks (in performSearch lines 404-406 and inside loadEmbeddingStatus lines 489-491 and 494-496). The service request `mode` becomes the literal `"keyword"` (EngramServiceSearchRequest.mode is a required String; CommandPaletteView already passes `mode: "keyword"` the same way at line 204). The `SearchMode` enum + `SearchMode.availableModes(...)` in SearchSupport.swift and its SearchModeTests stay untouched — SearchSupport.swift is outside this WP's file ownership, the enum is still the documented keyword-only guard, and removing the UI does not orphan the enum at the type level (it is still referenced by the type system via SearchResult and remains test-covered). The pre-existing now-unreachable `.semantic`/`.hybrid` enum cases and the purple/green branches of `modeColor`/`matchBadge` (lines 503, 515-516) are flagged-but-kept (pre-existing dead code, not created by this change).

(2) search-3 / remove-misleading — delete the embedding-status pill. Remove `@State embeddingStatus` (line 62), the `loadEmbeddingStatus()` func (lines 479-498), its `await loadEmbeddingStatus()` call in `.task` (line 103), and the green-dot 'N/M embedded' HStack (lines 160-167). After both (1) and (2), the `HStack(spacing: 12) { … Spacer() … }` wrapper at lines 140-168 has lost both its mode-pill block and its embedding-pill block, leaving only a bare `Spacer()`; remove the entire wrapper HStack. The `EmbeddingStatus` struct (SearchSupport.swift) and `serviceClient.embeddingStatus()` (EngramServiceClient.swift) are NOT edited by this WP. Correction to the original spec's justification: they are NOT kept "because Home/Popover use them" — Home/Popover read `serviceStatusStore.embeddingStatus` (a String on EngramServiceStatusStore), not this struct or this client method. After this WP, SearchPageView was the ONLY remaining app-target consumer of both, so both become orphaned in the app target. They are left in place (no compile break: the struct lives in SearchSupport.swift, the client method is still exercised by the service command handler, MockEngramServiceClient, and tests) and flagged as now-orphaned-in-app, pre-existing surfaces outside this WP's file ownership.

(3) xc-states-4 + command-palette-5 / new-ui — model the search result-state as one internal enum so the double-fault is a first-class state, not silent. Add `enum SearchOutcome: Equatable { case empty, results, failed }` at file scope in SearchPageView.swift (internal, so EngramTests can assert on it via `@testable import Engram`) with a pure classifier `static func classify(query:results:didFail:) -> SearchOutcome` (didFail wins over a non-empty stale results set). Add `@State searchFailed = false`. In performSearch: reset `searchFailed = false` at the top; in the inner-catch double-fault (the local-FTS fallback throws, lines 452-454) set `searchFailed = true` and `results = []` (guarded by `!Task.isCancelled`). In searchContent, drive the results section off SearchOutcome.classify(query:results:didFail:searchFailed) and add a distinct branch ahead of the existing 'No results' branch (line 199): when `.failed`, render EmptyState(icon: 'exclamationmark.triangle', title 'Search unavailable', message 'Could not reach the index. Try again.'). Also reset `searchFailed = false` in the clear-button action (line 129) and when the success path returns. Apply the identical fix in CommandPaletteView: add `@State searchFailed = false`; reset it before the service call; in the catch, after the `try? db.search` fallback, set `searchFailed = true` when the fallback yielded nothing after a service error; add a 'Search unavailable' branch ahead of the existing 'No results' branch (line 104-114). Because the palette computes `visibleItems.isEmpty` and has no internal classify seam, the palette change is view-local @State only (not unit-tested — see testPlan).

(4) test-fix / in-scope-required — AppSearchServiceCutoverScanTests.swift `testSearchPageDoesNotAdvertiseUnavailableSemanticModes` (lines 113-133) asserts the PRESENCE of the controls this WP deletes: line 116-119 `XCTAssertTrue(searchPage.contains("SearchMode.availableModes"))` and line 120-123 `XCTAssertTrue(searchPage.contains("selectedMode: SearchMode = .keyword"))`. Both fail the moment SearchPageView is edited. Remove those two `XCTAssertTrue` guards. Keep the two `XCTAssertFalse` guards (no `ForEach(SearchMode.allCases`, no 'Hybrid search combines keyword') — still valid and still green — and keep the sibling `testSwiftSearchPathStaysKeywordOnly`'s `mode: "hybrid"`/`mode: "semantic"` XCTAssertFalse checks valid (request mode is now the literal "keyword"). This file is added to WP04's ownership for this WP only, scoped to deleting those two assertions.
- **Changes:**
  - `edit` `macos/Engram/Views/Pages/SearchPageView.swift` — Remove dead mode selector: @State selectedMode (line 51), availableModes computed (65-67), mode-pill ForEach block (141-158), and the two availableModes.contains reset blocks (404-406, 489-496). Hardcode the service request mode: "keyword" (replacing selectedMode.rawValue at line 414). Remove embedding pill: @State embeddingStatus (62), loadEmbeddingStatus func (479-498), its .task call (103), and the green-dot N/M-embedded HStack (160-167); collapse the now-empty wrapper HStack(spacing:12) (140-168) since only a bare Spacer remains. Add internal SearchOutcome enum + classify(query:results:didFail:) at file scope; add @State searchFailed=false; reset searchFailed=false at top of performSearch, in the clear-button action, and on the success path; set searchFailed=true & results=[] in the inner (double-fault) catch (452-454); render a distinct 'Search unavailable' EmptyState (icon exclamationmark.triangle) driven by SearchOutcome ahead of the existing 'No results' branch (199).
  - `edit` `macos/Engram/Views/CommandPaletteView.swift` — Add @State searchFailed=false; reset it before the serviceClient.search call in performSearch (line 202); in the catch (215-228) set searchFailed=true when the db.search fallback yields nothing after the service error; add a 'Search unavailable' empty-state branch ahead of the existing 'No results' branch (104-114) so a backend failure is no longer indistinguishable from a genuine no-match. Command mode ('>' prefix) is unaffected.
  - `edit` `macos/EngramTests/AppSearchServiceCutoverScanTests.swift` — In testSearchPageDoesNotAdvertiseUnavailableSemanticModes remove the two now-invalid XCTAssertTrue guards: contains("SearchMode.availableModes") (116-119) and contains("selectedMode: SearchMode = .keyword") (120-123), since this WP deletes both from SearchPageView. Keep the two XCTAssertFalse guards (no ForEach(SearchMode.allCases; no 'Hybrid search combines keyword') and the sibling mode: "hybrid"/"semantic" XCTAssertFalse checks unchanged and green.
  - `create` `macos/EngramTests/SearchOutcomeTests.swift` — New XCTest (@testable import Engram) asserting SearchPageView's file-scope SearchOutcome.classify: empty/whitespace query -> .empty; non-empty query + non-empty results + didFail=false -> .results; non-empty query + empty results + didFail=true -> .failed (the double-fault regression guard); didFail=true + non-empty (stale) results -> .failed (failure takes precedence over leftover rows).
- **APIs used:**
  - `EngramServiceClient.search` (macos/Shared/Service/EngramServiceClient.swift) `func search(_ request: EngramServiceSearchRequest) async throws -> EngramServiceSearchResponse` ✓
  - `EngramServiceSearchRequest.init` (macos/Shared/Service/EngramServiceModels.swift) `init(query: String, mode: String, limit: Int, project: String? = nil, source: String? = nil, since: String? = nil)` ✓
  - `EngramServiceSearchResponse.Item.searchResult` (macos/Engram/Views/SearchSupport.swift) `var searchResult: SearchResult  // maps service item -> SearchResult (KEPT, not edited)` ✓
  - `SearchMode.availableModes` (macos/Engram/Views/SearchSupport.swift) `static func availableModes(embeddingAvailable: Bool) -> [SearchMode]  // returns [.keyword]; KEPT, outside WP04 file ownership` ✓
  - `EmbeddingStatus` (macos/Engram/Views/SearchSupport.swift) `struct EmbeddingStatus { let available: Bool; let model: String?; let embeddedCount: Int; let totalSessions: Int; let progress: Int }  // KEPT (not edited); after this WP it is orphaned in the app target — flagged, pre-existing, outside WP04 ownership` ✓
  - `EngramServiceClient.embeddingStatus` (macos/Shared/Service/EngramServiceClient.swift) `func embeddingStatus() async throws -> EngramServiceEmbeddingStatusResponse  // KEPT (not edited); SearchPageView was its last app-target caller, but it is still exercised by the service command handler, MockEngramServiceClient, and tests — no compile break` ✓
  - `EngramServiceStatusStore.embeddingStatus` (macos/Shared/Service/EngramServiceStatusStore.swift) `var embeddingStatus: String?  // the property Home/Popover actually read — NOT the SearchSupport EmbeddingStatus struct; untouched by this WP` ✓
  - `EmptyState.init` (macos/Engram/Components/EmptyState.swift) `struct EmptyState: View { let icon: String; let title: String; let message: String; var action: (label: String, action: () -> Void)? = nil }  // title/message are LocalizedStringKey-rendered` ✓
  - `DatabaseManager.searchWithSnippets` (macos/Engram/Core/Database.swift) `searchWithSnippets(query:limit:sources:projects:since:) -> [...]  // called in the existing SearchPageView fallback (line 438); unchanged` ⚠ UNCONFIRMED
  - `DatabaseManager.search` (macos/Engram/Core/Database.swift) `db.search(query:limit:) -> [Session]  // called in CommandPaletteView fallback (line 218); unchanged` ⚠ UNCONFIRMED
  - `SessionBox.init` (macos/Engram/AppNotifications.swift) `init(_ session: Session)  // single-arg today (AppNotifications.swift:11-17). NOT edited by this WP — the query-carry change was dropped; AppNotifications.swift is owned by no WP` ✓
- **UX behavior:** SearchPageView states:
- Empty query: unchanged 'Search sessions' EmptyState (classify -> .empty).
- Searching: unchanged spinner + 'Searching…'.
- Results found: unchanged '{n} results' + list (classify -> .results). The mode-selector pill row and the 'N/M embedded' green-dot pill no longer render at all (deleted permanently, not hidden). The active-modes pill row (e.g. 'keyword' / 'keyword (offline)') driven by response.searchModes is KEPT — it is the honest signal that a result set came from the live service vs the local FTS fallback.
- Genuine no-match (service or local FTS returned [] without error): unchanged 'No results — Try a different search term or mode' (classify -> .empty with non-empty query).
- Double-fault (service threw AND local FTS threw): NEW (classify -> .failed). Shows EmptyState(icon: exclamationmark.triangle, title 'Search unavailable', message 'Could not reach the index. Try again.'); any prior results are cleared (results=[]) so no stale rows mislead. Clearing the field or a successful later search resets searchFailed.

CommandPaletteView states:
- Empty query: unchanged 'Type to search sessions'.
- Searching: unchanged inline ProgressView.
- Genuine no-match: unchanged 'No results' + 'Type > for navigation commands'.
- Backend failure (service error then db.search fallback yields nothing): NEW 'Search unavailable' state distinct from 'No results', so a down socket / broken index no longer reads as 'your data is missing'. Command mode ('>' prefix) is unaffected (never hits the search backend).

Edge cases: SearchPageView query length < 2 still short-circuits (no request, results=[]); searchFailed is reset before every attempt so a transient failure clears on the next keystroke; Task cancellation guards are preserved (no state mutation after cancel, including no searchFailed write after cancel).
- **Acceptance:**
  - SearchPageView no longer renders any keyword/semantic/hybrid mode-selector pill under any condition (the gated block, @State selectedMode, and availableModes computed are deleted, not just unreachable).
  - SearchPageView no longer calls serviceClient.embeddingStatus(), no longer holds @State embeddingStatus, and no longer renders the 'N/M embedded' green-dot pill; loadEmbeddingStatus and its .task call are removed.
  - The service search request from SearchPageView uses mode: "keyword" literally; the project builds with selectedMode/availableModes removed.
  - When both serviceClient.search and the local FTS fallback throw, SearchPageView shows a 'Search unavailable' EmptyState (icon exclamationmark.triangle) and clears stale results instead of 'No results'.
  - CommandPaletteView shows a distinct 'Search unavailable' state (not 'No results') when the service search errors and the db.search fallback yields nothing.
  - AppSearchServiceCutoverScanTests.testSearchPageDoesNotAdvertiseUnavailableSemanticModes passes after dropping the two presence assertions (SearchMode.availableModes; selectedMode: SearchMode = .keyword); its XCTAssertFalse guards and testSwiftSearchPathStaysKeywordOnly remain green.
  - SearchMode enum, SearchMode.availableModes, EmbeddingStatus struct (all in SearchSupport.swift), serviceClient.embeddingStatus(), and existing SearchModeTests remain present and passing — none are edited by this WP.
  - SearchOutcomeTests passes: .empty / .results / .failed classify correctly and didFail wins over a non-empty stale results set.
- **Test plan:** Add macos/EngramTests/SearchOutcomeTests.swift (XCTest, @testable import Engram) covering the new file-scope SearchPageView SearchOutcome.classify(query:results:didFail:): (a) empty/whitespace query -> .empty; (b) non-empty query + non-empty results + didFail=false -> .results; (c) non-empty query + empty results + didFail=true -> .failed (the double-fault regression guard, the core of xc-states-4/command-palette-5); (d) didFail=true + non-empty (stale) results -> .failed (failure takes precedence over leftover rows). Construct fake SearchResult values via SearchResult(id:session:snippet:matchType:score:) (session may be nil). Update macos/EngramTests/AppSearchServiceCutoverScanTests.swift by deleting the two XCTAssertTrue presence assertions that this WP makes false (the source-scan test continues to enforce that no hybrid/semantic mode is requested or advertised). The CommandPaletteView 'Search unavailable' branch and the SearchPageView @State searchFailed wiring are SwiftUI @State and are not unit-testable in this harness; the testable seam is the pure SearchOutcome classifier the SearchPageView body branches on — consistent with the existing SnippetHighlighterTests pattern of testing pure helpers in the view layer. The existing SearchModeTests.swift stays unchanged as the guard that availableModes is keyword-only.
- **Risks:** No cross-WP compile coupling remains: the SessionBox query-carry line was dropped from this WP, so nothing in WP04 depends on an unowned edit to AppNotifications.swift. The mandatory in-scope risk is the cutover scan test — if change (4) is skipped, AppSearchServiceCutoverScanTests breaks the moment SearchPageView is edited; this WP fixes it in the same change set, so there is no CI regression. Removals are confined to unreachable/dead UI; EmbeddingStatus/embeddingStatus()/SearchMode are not edited and stay intact for their real (non-app or test) consumers, so no other view or test breaks. After this WP, the EmbeddingStatus struct and serviceClient.embeddingStatus() are orphaned in the app target — flagged for a future cleanup WP, not deleted here (out of file ownership; no compile break). The new error state is additive. modeColor/matchBadge keep now-dead semantic branches (pre-existing, flagged not deleted).
- **Out of scope:** Does NOT build semantic/vector/hybrid search — CLAUDE.md states sqlite-vec is not implemented; the honest fix is removal, not backend work. Does NOT touch SearchSupport.swift (SearchMode enum, availableModes, EmbeddingStatus struct, searchResult mapping) or the embeddingStatus() client method or EngramServiceStatusStore — outside file ownership and still used elsewhere (service handler / tests). Does NOT remove the Home/Popover 'embedding STATUS' rows — those read serviceStatusStore.embeddingStatus (a String), are a different surface, and are out of scope. DROPS the original spec's change (4) query-carry: passing the active query through SessionBox requires adding `query: String? = nil` to SessionBox.init in macos/Engram/AppNotifications.swift (note: the real path is macos/Engram/AppNotifications.swift, NOT macos/Engram/Views/AppNotifications.swift as the original spec stated), and that file is owned by no work-package and is NOT in WP03's file list (WP03 owns SessionDetailView/TranscriptFindBar/TranscriptText/SearchSupport/TranscriptFindTests). Re-scope the query-carry as a separate cross-cutting handoff that (a) assigns an owner to AppNotifications.swift, (b) adds the optional defaulted param + a query property to SessionBox (safe — all ~10 existing single-arg call sites keep compiling), and (c) consumes it in MainWindowView/SessionDetailView find-bar priming. This WP deliberately does not emit the query, so the SessionBox(session) call at SearchPageView.swift:222 is left unchanged.

### WP05 — Replay backfill: populate role/timestamps/tool-calls so density bar and playback timing are real

- **Disposition:** backfill-data  ·  **Critique:** needs-revision (revised)
- **Closes:** replay-1, replay-2, replay-3, replay-5
- **Goal:** Make Session Replay's three differentiating value-adds (role coloring, time-density heatmap, data-driven playback pacing) actually function by sourcing the replay timeline from the real per-message adapter stream (role + timestamp + token usage + tool calls) instead of reverse-parsing the role-less FTS blob, stop the summary appearing as a phantom trailing entry, AND make the client-side density-bar timestamp parser tolerant of non-fractional ISO8601 so the heatmap lights up for sources that emit non-fractional timestamps.
- **Approach:** Root cause confirmed by reading the code: SQLiteEngramServiceReadProvider.replayTimeline (EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:630-674) reads `SELECT rowid, content FROM sessions_fts WHERE session_id = ?` and feeds each row to replayRoleAndPreview (:918-928), which only matches literal \"User:\"/\"Assistant:\"/\"Tool:\" prefixes. But IndexJobRunner.buildSearchContent writes raw `message.content` with NO prefix, filters to user/assistant only, and appends the summary as a trailing line. So every entry resolves to role \"unknown\"/default-tool-color (replay-1), all timestamps/tokens/durations are nil (replay-2), tool messages never exist in FTS (replay-3), and the summary is a phantom final entry (replay-5).\n\nThe fix is NOT to add role prefixes into FTS (that would pollute keyword search content and still lack timestamps/tokens). Instead, re-source the replay read path from the same adapter stream that already carries everything: NormalizedMessage (SessionAdapter.swift) has role (incl. .tool), content, timestamp, toolCalls ([NormalizedToolCall].name), and usage (TokenUsage.inputTokens/outputTokens). The read provider already streams messages from disk in this exact module: resumeTranscriptContextLines (EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:1315-1327) shows the precedent — it does NOT stream inside the GRDB read{} block; it awaits an async reader OUTSIDE the block. I will follow that precedent exactly.\n\nIMPLEMENTATION SHAPE (explicit so the implementer does not stream inside read{}): replayTimeline first calls read{} to fetch ONLY Sendable scalars — source and the COALESCE'd readable locator using the SAME expression as IndexJobRunner.sessionContentSource:271-277 (COALESCE(NULLIF(ls.local_readable_path,''), NULLIF(s.file_path,''), s.source_locator) with LEFT JOIN session_local_state). Then, OUTSIDE the read{} block (the method is already async), it resolves the adapter via SessionAdapterFactory.defaultAdapters().first(where:{ $0.source == source }) (same lookup TranscriptExportService.swift:372 uses in this module), conditionally downcasts to MessageAdapter, and awaits adapter.streamMessages(locator:options: StreamMessagesOptions(limit:)) collecting NormalizedMessages (incl. .tool role). The read() helper (:937) runs a synchronous @Sendable block on a blocking queue and CANNOT await an async stream — so streaming MUST be outside it.\n\nI will NOT use ServiceTranscriptReader because its isDefaultVisibleMessage filter drops tool messages — which would defeat replay-3. The collected NormalizedMessages are converted with a NEW pure static `replayEntries(from messages: [ReplayMessage], limit:)` where ReplayMessage is a small Sendable mirror of (role, content, timestamp, toolName, inputTokens, outputTokens).\n\nTOOLNAME DATA SOURCE (corrected per critique — verified in adapters): toolName on a ReplayMessage is populated from `message.toolCalls?.first?.name`, applied to WHATEVER message carries toolCalls — NOT keyed to the .tool role. This matters because the two emit patterns differ: ClaudeCodeAdapter.message (ClaudeCodeAdapter.swift:356,365,370) attaches toolCalls to the ASSISTANT turn (the tool_use blocks) and emits a SEPARATE .tool-role record for the tool_result that carries toolCalls=nil; whereas CodexAdapter (CodexAdapter.swift:493-501) emits role=.tool for a function_call WITH toolCalls=[NormalizedToolCall(name:)] on that same .tool row. So for ClaudeCode the tool NAME surfaces on the assistant entry; for Codex it surfaces on the tool entry. Either way, sourcing toolName from message.toolCalls?.first?.name (independent of role) captures the name wherever the adapter put it. durationToNextMs is computed by diffing consecutive ISO timestamps (ms, clamped >=0, nil when either side is missing/unparseable). Summary is never appended, so replay-5 disappears for free.\n\nWhen the locator is empty / sync:// / adapter missing or not a MessageAdapter / file unreadable / stream throws, fall back to the existing FTS-derived entries (keeping ReplayFTSRow + the old replayEntries(from:source:limit:) overload, and the in-function sessions_fts query) so synced-only sessions still show a (role-less) timeline rather than going blank — graceful degradation, not regression.\n\nDENSITY-BAR PARSER FIX (corrected per critique — this is now a REAL edit, not a no-op): ReplayState.isoFormatter (ReplayState.swift:26-30) sets formatOptions=[.withInternetDateTime, .withFractionalSeconds], which FAILS to parse timestamps WITHOUT fractional seconds (e.g. '2026-06-14T10:00:00Z'). Adapter timestamps come straight from source files; many sources emit non-fractional ISO. With the old all-nil data this never mattered, but once real timestamps flow, a session whose first/last timestamps lack fractional seconds would make densityBuckets (:63-90) return 100 zeros (flat bar) — silently re-breaking replay-2 for those sources. The fix is to make the client-side parse tolerant of BOTH formats: replace the single strict ISO8601DateFormatter with a parse helper that tries fractional-seconds first, then non-fractional ([.withInternetDateTime] only). densityBuckets keeps its exact bucketing math; only the date-from-string call changes to the tolerant helper. This is the minimal change that makes replay-2's heatmap real for all sources rather than only fractional-timestamp ones.\n\nReplayState.densityBuckets and scheduleNext (:131-151, cap 3.0s :141) and SessionReplayView's timestamp/token labels (:197-207) already consume timestamp/tokens/durationToNextMs correctly — they were dead only because the data is nil. So those consumers need no logic change beyond the formatter tolerance fix. SessionReplayView.loadTimeline (:240-251) already maps entry.tokens as input+output and durationToNextMs, so the client mapping is ready. The only view-side gap: roleColor default branch (:225-231) returns MessageType.tool.color for ANY non-user/non-assistant role, so a genuinely role-\"unknown\" FTS-fallback entry mis-renders as a tool. Add an explicit \"tool\" case and let the default return a neutral secondary color so fallback \"unknown\" entries are not mislabeled as tools.
- **Changes:**
  - `edit` `macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceReadProvider.swift` — Rewrite SQLiteEngramServiceReadProvider.replayTimeline (:630-674) to source from the adapter stream. Step 1: read{} fetches ONLY Sendable scalars — source + COALESCE(NULLIF(ls.local_readable_path,''),NULLIF(s.file_path,''),s.source_locator) via LEFT JOIN session_local_state (same expression as IndexJobRunner.sessionContentSource:271-277), plus the FTS fallback rows/total so a single read covers both paths. Step 2 (OUTSIDE the read{} block, since the method is async and read() cannot await — precedent resumeTranscriptContextLines:1315-1327): if the locator is non-empty and not sync://, resolve the adapter via SessionAdapterFactory.defaultAdapters().first(where:{ $0.source == source }) (same lookup as :372), downcast to MessageAdapter, and try await adapter.streamMessages(locator:options: StreamMessagesOptions(limit:)) collecting into [ReplayMessage]; map toolName from message.toolCalls?.first?.name (independent of role), role from NormalizedMessageRole.rawValue, tokens from usage.inputTokens/outputTokens. Convert via the NEW pure static replayEntries(from:[ReplayMessage],limit:). On any throw / missing adapter / empty locator / sync:// / zero streamed messages, fall back to the existing Self.replayEntries(from: ftsRows, source:, limit:). totalEntries reflects streamed count on the happy path; hasMore = total > entries.count. Keep the existing ReplayFTSRow struct (:893), the FTS replayEntries(from:source:limit:) overload (:898-916), replayRoleAndPreview (:918), and an in-function sessions_fts query (so the existing IPC structural test still sees `sessions_fts` and never `fileSystemProvider.replayTimeline`). Add a small Sendable ReplayMessage struct (role:String, content:String, timestamp:String?, toolName:String?, inputTokens:Int?, outputTokens:Int?). Do NOT append summary. COORDINATION: this file is co-owned with WP13 (which edits the disjoint sources() method); land WP05's replayTimeline rewrite FIRST, then WP13 rebases — disjoint methods, no textual line overlap, but sequence to avoid a merge hazard.
  - `edit` `macos/Engram/Models/ReplayState.swift` — Make the density-bar timestamp parse tolerant of non-fractional ISO8601. Replace the single strict isoFormatter (:26-30, formatOptions=[.withInternetDateTime,.withFractionalSeconds]) usage with a small static parse helper `parseISO(_:) -> Date?` that tries a fractional-seconds formatter first, then a non-fractional one ([.withInternetDateTime]). Update densityBuckets (:69-71,:84) to call parseISO instead of isoFormatter.date(from:). Keep ALL bucketing math, the count>=2 / first / last guards, and the totalDuration<=0 branch exactly as-is. No new fields on ReplayTimelineEntry (it already has timestamp/tokens/durationToNextMs :4-13). This is the only behavioral edit here and it is required so replay-2's heatmap renders for sources emitting non-fractional timestamps.
  - `edit` `macos/Engram/Views/Replay/SessionReplayView.swift` — roleColor(_:) (:225-231): add an explicit `case "tool": return MessageType.tool.color` and change the default branch to return a neutral secondary color (e.g. Theme.textSecondary / .secondary equivalent already used in this view) so a literally-"unknown"-role entry (only possible in the FTS fallback path) renders neutrally instead of being mislabeled as a tool. Keep user/assistant mapping. No other view change — timestamp/token/density UI is already correct (:185-207).
  - `create` `macos/EngramServiceCoreTests/ReplayDataTests.swift` — New XCTest file (declared owned by WP05). (1) Unit-test the new pure replayEntries(from:[ReplayMessage],limit:): roles preserved (user/assistant/tool), toolName carried from ReplayMessage.toolName, timestamps passed through, tokens mapped to Tokens(input,output), durationToNextMs computed from consecutive ISO timestamps and nil at the tail / when a neighbor timestamp is missing, summary NOT appended (count == message count, capped at limit). (2) Density-parser test for the ReplayState formatter tolerance: build a ReplayState, set entries with NON-FRACTIONAL timestamps ('2026-06-14T10:00:00Z' ... '2026-06-14T10:10:00Z') clustered, assert densityBuckets is non-flat (sum>0 and not all in one bucket); repeat with fractional timestamps to prove both formats parse. (3) End-to-end: seed a sessions row (source='codex') whose file_path points at a temp .jsonl fixture containing a user line, an assistant line with usage, and a Codex function_call line (which carries toolCalls=[name]) — all with timestamps in a format the tolerant parser accepts (include one non-fractional case); build SQLiteEngramServiceReadProvider over that temp DB; await replayTimeline; assert entries have non-nil timestamps, a role=="tool" entry exists with toolName populated (Codex puts the name on the tool row), totalEntries==3, and no entry whose preview equals the session summary. NOTE for the fixture author: if a ClaudeCode fixture is used instead, the toolName assertion must target the ASSISTANT entry (ClaudeCode attaches toolCalls to the assistant turn, not the .tool-result row). (4) Fallback test: session with empty/sync:// locator + seeded sessions_fts rows still returns FTS-derived entries (role may be "unknown"), proving graceful degradation rather than empty/error.
- **APIs used:**
  - `SQLiteEngramServiceReadProvider.replayTimeline(_:)` (macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceReadProvider.swift) `func replayTimeline(_ request: EngramServiceReplayTimelineRequest) async throws -> EngramServiceReplayTimelineResponse` ✓
  - `SQLiteEngramServiceReadProvider.replayEntries(from:source:limit:)` (macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceReadProvider.swift) `static func replayEntries(from rows: [ReplayFTSRow], source: String?, limit: Int) -> [EngramServiceReplayTimelineEntry]` ✓

  - `SQLiteEngramServiceReadProvider.resumeTranscriptContextLines (streaming-outside-read precedent)` (macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceReadProvider.swift) `private static func resumeTranscriptContextLines(filePath: String, source: String) async -> [String] — awaits ServiceTranscriptReader.readMessages OUTSIDE any read{} block (:1315-1327)` ✓

  - `ClaudeCodeAdapter.message(from:) tool/toolCalls emission` (macos/Shared/EngramCore/Adapters/Sources/ClaudeCodeAdapter.swift) `role=.tool ONLY for user-record tool_result (:361,365); toolCalls attached to the ASSISTANT message (:356,370); a .tool-role record carries toolCalls=nil — so toolName surfaces on the assistant entry` ✓

  - `ReplayState.densityBuckets / scheduleNext / isoFormatter` (macos/Engram/Models/ReplayState.swift) `isoFormatter formatOptions=[.withInternetDateTime,.withFractionalSeconds] (:26-30) — FAILS non-fractional ISO; densityBuckets guards first/last timestamp (:62-90); scheduleNext uses durationToNextMs ?? 500 capped at 3.0s (:131-151)` ✓
  - `SessionReplayView.roleColor / loadTimeline` (macos/Engram/Views/Replay/SessionReplayView.swift) `roleColor default → MessageType.tool.color (:225-231, mis-colors unknown); loadTimeline maps tokens.map{ $0.input+$0.output } and durationToNextMs (:240-251)` ✓
  - `EngramServiceClient.replayTimeline(sessionId:limit:)` (macos/Shared/Service/EngramServiceClient.swift) `func replayTimeline(sessionId: String, limit: Int?) async throws -> EngramServiceReplayTimelineResponse` ✓
- **UX behavior:** Loading: SessionReplayView already shows a ProgressView while replayState.isLoading (unchanged). Happy path (local-readable claude-code/codex/etc. session): each entry shows its real role badge — User/Assistant/Tool with the correct color (MessageType colors); the per-message timestamp label (:197-201) and token label (:203-207) render because timestamp/tokens are now non-nil; the density bar renders a real heatmap (buckets reflect message clustering over wall-clock time) instead of a flat strip, NOW INCLUDING sources that emit non-fractional ISO timestamps (the formatter-tolerance fix); Play advances at the session's real cadence because durationToNextMs is populated (capped at 3s per scheduleNext). Tool-call entries now appear in the timeline (previously absent): for Codex the tool entry itself carries toolName; for ClaudeCode the tool_result entry shows role Tool while the tool NAME is carried on the preceding Assistant entry (where the adapter attaches toolCalls). The phantom trailing summary entry is gone, so progress reads N/N matching real turns. Empty state: zero parseable messages → entries empty → existing 'No timeline data' empty state. Error state: stream/parse failure on the adapter path is caught and the provider falls back to FTS-derived entries; only if BOTH fail does it return empty. Service/IPC error surfaces via existing catch → replayState.error → warning panel. Edge cases: (a) synced-only / sync:// locator or missing file_path → FTS fallback timeline (role-less, no timestamps; density flat, pacing 500ms default — the OLD behavior, preserved as graceful degradation, never worse than today); (b) messages with no timestamps → durationToNextMs nil → uniform pacing for that gap; (c) a session whose first/last message lack timestamps returns flat (densityBuckets guard needs first AND last) — acceptable, matches existing guard; (d) large sessions bounded by limit (default 500, cap 2000) via StreamMessagesOptions(limit:). FTS-fallback role-'unknown' entries render with a neutral secondary color (not tool color) after the roleColor tweak.
- **Acceptance:**
  - Opening Replay on a locally-readable claude-code/codex session shows User/Assistant/Tool role badges with distinct colors (no entry labeled 'Unknown' on the happy path).
  - Tool-call messages appear as entries (role 'tool'); toolName is populated wherever the adapter carries toolCalls — on the Codex tool entry, and on the preceding ClaudeCode Assistant entry.
  - Per-entry timestamp and token labels render for messages that carry them.
  - The density bar shows a non-uniform heatmap for a session with clustered activity, for BOTH fractional and non-fractional ISO timestamps (formatter tolerance), not a flat 100-zeros bar.
  - Play pacing varies with real inter-message gaps (durationToNextMs populated), still capped at 3s.
  - The session summary no longer appears as a trailing timeline entry; progress N/N equals real turn count.
  - A synced-only / missing-file / sync:// session still returns a (degraded, role-less) timeline via FTS fallback rather than going blank or erroring.
  - New replayEntries(from:[ReplayMessage],limit:) computes durationToNextMs from consecutive timestamps, nil at the tail and when a neighbor timestamp is missing, and never appends a summary; covered by a unit test.
  - ReplayState density-parser tolerates non-fractional ISO8601 (e.g. '2026-06-14T10:00:00Z'); covered by a test asserting non-flat buckets for both formats.
  - Existing EngramServiceIPCTests.testReplayTimelineBuildsEntriesFromFtsRows and testSQLiteReplayTimelineDoesNotDelegateToEmptyFileSystemStub still pass UNCHANGED (the FTS overload and an in-function sessions_fts query are retained; replayTimeline never delegates to fileSystemProvider.replayTimeline).
- **Test plan:** Add macos/EngramServiceCoreTests/ReplayDataTests.swift (owned by WP05): (1) testReplayEntriesFromMessagesPreservesRolesAndComputesDurations — call the new pure static replayEntries(from:[ReplayMessage],limit:) with user(ts=T0), assistant(ts=T0+1500ms, tokens in/out, toolName='Bash' to mirror ClaudeCode), tool(ts=T0+5000ms, toolName nil); assert roles==[user,assistant,tool], the assistant entry has toolName=='Bash', durationToNextMs==[1500,3500,nil], tokens mapped, count==3 (no summary). (2) testReplayEntriesNilDurationWhenTimestampMissing — middle message with nil timestamp → both neighbor durations nil. (3) testDensityParserToleratesNonFractionalISO — seed ReplayState.entries with non-fractional timestamps ('2026-06-14T10:00:00Z' clustered to ':10:00Z'); assert densityBuckets sum>0 and not concentrated in one bucket; repeat with fractional timestamps to prove both parse. (4) testReplayTimelineStreamsRealRolesEndToEnd — seed a sessions row (source='codex', file_path → temp .jsonl with a user line, an assistant line with usage, and a Codex function_call line carrying name='Bash', timestamps in a parser-accepted format incl. one non-fractional); build SQLiteEngramServiceReadProvider over that temp DB; await replayTimeline; assert >=1 entry role=='tool' with toolName=='Bash' (Codex puts name on the tool row), all timestamps non-nil, totalEntries==3, and no entry preview equals the session summary. (5) testReplayTimelineFallsBackToFtsWhenLocatorMissing — session with empty/sync:// file_path + seeded sessions_fts rows → entries still returned (role may be 'unknown'), proving graceful degradation. Do NOT edit EngramServiceIPCTests.swift — its two replay tests pass unchanged (verified: the FTS overload is retained and an in-function sessions_fts query remains, while the body never references fileSystemProvider.replayTimeline). Run: xcodebuild test -scheme Engram -only-testing:EngramServiceCoreTests/ReplayDataTests, and re-run the existing EngramServiceIPCTests replay cases to confirm they still pass.
- **Risks:** (1) Performance: replay now parses the transcript file on demand instead of reading pre-indexed FTS rows; bounded by StreamMessagesOptions(limit:) (default 500 / cap 2000). The DB row lookup stays on blockingReadQueue inside read{}; the streaming runs OUTSIDE read{} on the cooperative pool (per resumeTranscriptContextLines precedent), so it does not block the read queue. A very large transcript could still take longer than an FTS scan — acceptable for a user-initiated single-session view, bounded by limit. (2) Timestamp availability varies by adapter; sources that do not populate NormalizedMessage.timestamp degrade density/pacing to flat/uniform (the documented replay-2 fallback — never fake variation). (3) Timestamp FORMAT varies; the ReplayState parser-tolerance fix covers fractional vs non-fractional ISO8601, but a wholly non-ISO format (unlikely for the streamed sources) would still fail to parse → flat density for that session. Documented limitation, not a regression. (4) durationToNextMs from ISO diffing assumes monotonic non-decreasing timestamps; out-of-order timestamps are clamped to >=0 to avoid negative delays. (5) FILE CO-OWNERSHIP: EngramServiceReadProvider.swift is also edited by WP13 (sources()/source-pulse). The two edit disjoint methods (replayTimeline vs sources) so there is no textual overlap, but they are concurrent writers — LANDING ORDER: WP05 lands the replayTimeline rewrite first, WP13 rebases onto it. Flagged for coordination. (6) toolName half-closure risk is now closed: sourcing from message.toolCalls?.first?.name (role-independent) captures the name on whichever turn the adapter attaches it (assistant for ClaudeCode, tool for Codex), so the 'tool name shows' UX holds for both.
- **Out of scope:** DROPPED from the change set vs the original spec (per critique, minimum-diff): (a) IndexJobRunner.swift — the original spec admitted it was 'comment-only or no-op'; replay no longer reads FTS in the happy path, but adding a clarifying comment to a hot indexer file with its own test surface is a gratuitous diff. Not touched. buildSearchContent's user/assistant-only filter and summary append remain AS-IS — correct for KEYWORD SEARCH, out of scope to alter. (b) EngramServiceIPCTests.swift — NOT edited. Verified both replay tests pass unchanged: testReplayTimelineBuildsEntriesFromFtsRows exercises the RETAINED replayEntries(from:source:limit:) overload; testSQLiteReplayTimelineDoesNotDelegateToEmptyFileSystemStub asserts the body lacks 'fileSystemProvider.replayTimeline' (still true) and contains 'sessions_fts' (still true — the in-function fallback query is retained). Editing it would be undeclared-file churn. NOTE: the ReplayState.swift edit, which the ORIGINAL spec marked as a probable no-op, is RETAINED and is now a REAL edit (non-fractional ISO tolerance) because without it replay-2's density bar silently fails for non-fractional-timestamp sources. STILL out of scope: no new persisted messages table or new indexer write path (replay reads the transcript on demand, no schema migration); no pagination/offset for replay (limit suffices); no change to ReplayState's playback/density bucketing MATH beyond the date-parse call; no semantic search / embeddings.

### WP06 — Memory page: surface DB insights (list/read/save/delete) + full-file .md viewer + loading/refresh

- **Disposition:** wire-up  ·  **Critique:** needs-revision (revised)
- **Closes:** memory-insights-1, memory-insights-2, memory-insights-3, memory-insights-4, xc-capability-matrix-1-memory
- **Goal:** Make the advertised "Memory" feature usable from the GUI: surface the DB insights table (list + full text + save + delete) that is currently MCP-only, show the full content of memory .md files instead of a 200-char preview, and add loading/refresh feedback. All write paths reuse the existing token-gated EngramServiceClient.saveInsight / deleteInsight. The insights read and full-file content require one new read-only IPC command (`insights`) plus one optional model field (`content`). These shared-file service-plumbing edits are NOT owned by WP06 — they are extracted into a single serialized prerequisite (WP06-SVC) and WP06's UI depends on the resulting `EngramServiceClient.insights()` API and `EngramServiceMemoryFile.content` field.
- **Approach:** The four findings are facets of one gap: MemoryView only shows truncated filesystem .md previews and never touches the insights table, while a complete token-gated write API (saveInsight/deleteInsight) and the insights rows exist but have zero app callers.

OWNERSHIP RESOLUTION (the core revision the critique demanded). The original plan edited six files outside WP06's declared three-file ownership: EngramServiceModels.swift (owned by WP16), EngramServiceReadProvider.swift (owned by WP05 + WP13), EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift (owned by WP14), and Protocol/Client/Mock (unassigned). Editing those concurrently with their owners is a hard conflict. Resolution: factor all shared-file service-plumbing into a single serialized work item, WP06-SVC, which holds a serialized write-window on those files coordinated with WP16/WP05/WP13/WP14 (those WPs are notified; WP06-SVC lands after their structural edits or in an explicitly granted window). WP06 proper owns ONLY UI files (MemoryView.swift, the new InsightDetailView.swift, and its test file) and depends on WP06-SVC's API surface (`EngramServiceClient.insights()`, `EngramServiceMemoryFile.content`, `EngramServiceInsightInfo`). This converts six unilateral cross-owner edits into one scheduled dependency.

WRITE side (memory-insights-1) is pure wiring: EngramServiceClient.saveInsight / .deleteInsight already exist, are token-gated (ServiceCapabilityToken.protectedCommands lines 20/25 confirmed), and have service handlers (saveInsight :898 / deleteInsight :970). MemoryView adds a New Insight sheet calling saveInsight and a delete control calling deleteInsight, then reloads.

READ side (memory-insights-2) needs a new read path: there is NO insights-list method anywhere (get_insights → MCPInsightsTool is a COST summary; the only table reads are private). WP06-SVC adds one read method `insights()` to EngramServiceReadProvider returning the rows (SELECT id, content, wing, room, importance, created_at FROM insights ORDER BY created_at DESC LIMIT 500), guarded by tableExists("insights"). The guard is REQUIRED, not defensive: ensureInsightTables (EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:738) creates the `insights` table LAZILY, only inside saveInsight/deleteInsight writes — on a fresh DB where no insight was ever saved the table does not exist, so an unguarded SELECT throws "no such table". This mirrors embeddingStatus's tableExists("session_embeddings") guard at :679. Rows are mapped to EngramServiceInsightInfo INSIDE the read{} block because a GRDB Row is not Sendable and cannot cross the blocking-read queue hop (explicit comment at :706-707; resumeCommand follows the same pattern).

FULL-FILE viewer (memory-insights-3): EngramServiceMemoryFile carries only `preview = content.prefixString(200)` (FileSystem provider :185) with no full-content field. WP06-SVC adds an optional `let content: String?` to EngramServiceMemoryFile and populates it from the already-read `content` string in FileSystemEngramServiceReadProvider.memoryFiles() (the provider already does String(contentsOf:) at :178 — zero extra I/O). content MUST be optional: the existing, WP06-unowned testStage3 round-trip (EngramServiceClientTests.swift:68-69) sends a memoryFiles payload with NO content field; a non-optional field would break that already-passing test. The SQLite provider delegates memoryFiles to the FileSystem provider (:623), so the population lives only in the FileSystem impl. MemoryView renders `selected.content ?? selected.preview` in the detail pane (drops the truncation); list rows keep preview.

LOADING/REFRESH (memory-insights-4, xc-capability-matrix-1-memory): add a ProgressView when isLoading && both lists empty, and a refresh button calling loadData(). After every save/delete, re-run loadData() so the change is reflected (also closes the "loads once, never refreshes" capability-matrix note).

InsightDetailView.swift (new UI file WP06 owns) holds the insight read-detail pane to keep MemoryView lean, mirroring the inlined file-detail pane.
- **Changes:**
  - `edit` `macos/Shared/Service/EngramServiceModels.swift` — [WP06-SVC, serialized with WP16] Add `struct EngramServiceInsightInfo: Codable, Equatable, Identifiable, Sendable` with fields: id:String, content:String, wing:String?, room:String?, importance:Int, createdAt:String? — plus an explicit `enum CodingKeys` mapping createdAt = "created_at" (matching the existing CodingKeys pattern on EngramServiceSaveInsightRequest :672). Drop sourceSessionId from the DTO (a raw session id is not meaningfully rendered by the detail pane; keeps the decode surface minimal per the critique). Add optional `let content: String?` to EngramServiceMemoryFile (MUST be optional so the existing memoryFiles payload in testStage3 — which has no content field — still decodes).
  - `edit` `macos/Shared/Service/EngramServiceProtocol.swift` — [WP06-SVC, file is unassigned in the map → WP06-SVC takes ownership] Add `func insights() async throws -> [EngramServiceInsightInfo]` to EngramServiceClientProtocol.
  - `edit` `macos/Shared/Service/EngramServiceClient.swift` — [WP06-SVC, unassigned → WP06-SVC owns] Add `func insights() async throws -> [EngramServiceInsightInfo] { try await command("insights") }` (no payload, mirrors sources()/skills()).
  - `edit` `macos/Shared/Service/MockEngramServiceClient.swift` — [WP06-SVC, unassigned → WP06-SVC owns] Add `let insightsResult: Result<[EngramServiceInsightInfo], Error>`, an `insights: [EngramServiceInsightInfo] = []` init param, `self.insightsResult = .success(insights)`, and `func insights() async throws -> [EngramServiceInsightInfo] { try insightsResult.get() }` to satisfy the protocol.
  - `edit` `macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceReadProvider.swift` — [WP06-SVC, serialized with WP05 + WP13] (1) Add `func insights() async throws -> [EngramServiceInsightInfo]` to the EngramServiceReadProvider protocol. (2) THREE conformers must implement it: EmptyEngramServiceReadProvider (:24) returns []; FileSystemEngramServiceReadProvider (:91) returns [] (no DB); SQLiteEngramServiceReadProvider (:399) runs `read { db in guard try tableExists("insights", db: db) else { return [] }; let rows = try Row.fetchAll(db, sql: "SELECT id, content, wing, room, importance, created_at FROM insights ORDER BY created_at DESC LIMIT 500"); return rows.map { EngramServiceInsightInfo(id:..., content:..., wing:..., room:..., importance: $0["importance"] ?? 5, createdAt: $0["created_at"] as String?) } }` — mapping rows to the Sendable DTO INSIDE the read{} block (Row is not Sendable, see :706-707). (3) In FileSystemEngramServiceReadProvider.memoryFiles() (:160-193), pass `content: content` into the EngramServiceMemoryFile initializer (the full `content` string is already read at :178); keep preview as-is. SQLite memoryFiles delegates to FileSystem (:623) so no change there.
  - `edit` `macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift` — [WP06-SVC, serialized with WP14] Add `case "insights": return .success(requestId: request.requestId, result: try Self.encode(try await readProvider.insights()))` to the dispatch switch, immediately after the `memoryFiles` case (:72-76) as the template. It is a READ — do NOT add it to ServiceCapabilityToken.protectedCommands.
  - `edit` `macos/Engram/Views/Pages/MemoryView.swift` — [WP06 owns] Add an Insights section above the memory-files list: @State insights:[EngramServiceInsightInfo]=[] loaded via serviceClient.insights() in loadData(); ForEach renders insight rows (content preview + wing/importance caption) as Buttons selecting into an @State selectedInsight that shows InsightDetailView; a 'New Insight' button presents a sheet (content TextEditor + importance stepper default 5, range 1...10) whose Save is enabled only when the extracted `MemoryView.insightContentIsValid(_:)` helper (trimmed count >= 10) is true, calling serviceClient.saveInsight(.init(content:..., wing:nil, room:nil, importance: Double(importance), sourceSessionId:nil, actor:"app")) then reloading; a row/context-menu Delete calling serviceClient.deleteInsight(.init(id:)) then reloading (clearing selectedInsight if it was the deleted one); a refresh (arrow.clockwise) button calling loadData(); a ProgressView when isLoading && memoryFiles.isEmpty && insights.isEmpty; change the file-detail Text to render the extracted `MemoryView.detailText(for:)` helper which returns selected.content ?? selected.preview (drop the prefix(200) truncation). Extract exactly TWO small pure static helpers — detailText(for:) and insightContentIsValid(_:) — no validator abstraction. loadData() awaits serviceClient.insights() and .memoryFiles() (these are async client calls, not DatabaseManager reads, so no Task.detached needed — matches the existing pattern at :93).
  - `create` `macos/Engram/Views/Memory/InsightDetailView.swift` — [WP06 owns; auto-included by xcodegen] New detail view taking an `insight: EngramServiceInsightInfo` and an `onDelete: () -> Void` closure. Renders full content (textSelection enabled), wing/room/importance/createdAt metadata captions, and a Delete button invoking onDelete. Pure presentation; no direct service calls. Renders every DTO field (wing, room, importance, createdAt) so none is dead — sourceSessionId was dropped from the DTO precisely because it had no render target.
  - `create` `macos/EngramTests/MemoryViewTests.swift` — [WP06 owns] XCTest, @testable import Engram. Three tests, all driven through the real client over RecordingServiceTransport (the harness MemoryView actually uses the concrete EngramServiceClient) plus the extracted pure helpers — NOT by injecting a mock into the SwiftUI view: (1) testInsightsCommandRoundTrips — EngramServiceClient over RecordingServiceTransport answering command "insights" with a one-element JSON array; assert client.insights() decodes id/content/importance and that createdAt maps from "created_at". (2) testMemoryFileOptionalContentAndDetailFallback — decode an EngramServiceMemoryFile JSON WITH content (assert MemoryView.detailText(for:) returns content) and one WITHOUT content (assert content==nil and detailText falls back to preview). (3) testInsightContentValidation — assert MemoryView.insightContentIsValid returns false for <10 trimmed chars and true for >=10.
- **APIs used:**

  - `MemoryView` (macos/Engram/Views/Pages/MemoryView.swift) `struct MemoryView: View with @Environment(EngramServiceClient.self) var serviceClient (concrete client, not protocol); loadData() awaits serviceClient.memoryFiles() directly (:93); detail pane currently renders selected.preview at :49` ✓
  - `MCPInsightsTool.result` (macos/EngramMCP/Core/MCPInsightsTool.swift) `static func result(database:since:) — produces a COST-insights summary, NOT the insights table; confirms get_insights is not a reusable insights-list read path` ⚠ UNCONFIRMED
- **UX behavior:** Memory page layout (top to bottom): search field (unchanged) → Insights section → Memory Files section (existing grouped-by-project list).

LOADING: on first open while both lists are empty, a centered ProgressView ("Loading memory…") shows instead of a blank page. Once loadData resolves, content or empty states appear.

INSIGHTS section: header "Insights" with a "+ New Insight" button and a refresh (arrow.clockwise) button. Each insight row shows the first ~2 lines of content plus a small wing/importance caption; tapping selects it into InsightDetailView (full content with textSelection, wing/room/importance/createdAt metadata, Delete button). Empty insights → EmptyState (icon "lightbulb", "No insights yet", "Save insights via save_insight or the New Insight button").

NEW INSIGHT: "+ New Insight" presents a sheet with a multiline content TextEditor, an importance stepper (default 5, 1–10), Cancel + Save. Save is disabled until the trimmed content is >= 10 chars (mirrors the service guard at EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:909 so there is no round-trip rejection). On Save: call serviceClient.saveInsight; on success dismiss sheet + reload (the new insight appears at top, created_at DESC). On failure keep the sheet open and show the inline error.localizedDescription. The service may return a "Similar insight already exists" dedup payload — treat as success and reload (the existing insight is already in the list).

DELETE: insight row context-menu "Delete" and a Delete button in InsightDetailView. On confirm, call serviceClient.deleteInsight(.init(id:)); on success reload, and if the deleted insight was selected clear the selection; on failure show AlertBanner with the error. No extra confirmation dialog (single-row delete, re-savable).

FULL-FILE VIEWER: tapping a memory .md file shows the FULL file content (content ?? preview) in the monospaced, scrollable, selectable detail pane — no 200-char cutoff. List rows keep the short preview.

REFRESH: the header refresh button re-runs loadData() (idempotent). After any save/delete, loadData() re-runs automatically so the page never shows stale data.

EDGE CASES: service busy/unavailable → loadData catch sets `error`, AlertBanner shows it, lists stay empty, ProgressView hidden. insights table absent (fresh DB, no insight ever saved) → insights() returns [] via the tableExists guard, shows the empty-insights state, no crash, no "no such table" error. content < 10 → Save disabled. memoryFiles payload without the new `content` field (older service version) → content is nil, detail falls back to preview, no regression on version skew.
- **Acceptance:**
  - MemoryView shows an Insights section listing rows from the insights table (id/content/wing/importance/createdAt) loaded via serviceClient.insights().
  - Tapping a memory .md file shows its FULL content (no 200-char truncation) via detailText(for:) = content ?? preview; list rows keep the short preview.
  - 'New Insight' sheet calls serviceClient.saveInsight and, on success, the new insight appears after an automatic reload; Save disabled until trimmed content >= 10 chars (insightContentIsValid).
  - An insight can be deleted via context-menu / InsightDetailView Delete button calling serviceClient.deleteInsight, and the list reloads removing it (selection cleared if it was selected).
  - A ProgressView shows while isLoading and both lists are empty; an empty-insights EmptyState shows when there are no insights and not loading.
  - A refresh control re-runs loadData(); save/delete also trigger an automatic reload.
  - Service/read errors surface via AlertBanner; insights() returns [] (no crash, no 'no such table') when the insights table is absent because the tableExists guard short-circuits.
  - EngramServiceMemoryFile.content is OPTIONAL so the existing testStage3 memoryFiles payload (no content field) still decodes and the viewer falls back to preview.
  - The new `insights` IPC command is a read and is NOT added to ServiceCapabilityToken.protectedCommands; saveInsight/deleteInsight remain token-gated.
  - All shared service-plumbing edits (Models, ReadProvider, CommandHandler, Protocol, Client, Mock) are landed under the serialized WP06-SVC window coordinated with WP16/WP05/WP13/WP14 — WP06's UI files do not concurrently edit any WP16/WP05/WP13/WP14-owned file.
- **Test plan:** Add macos/EngramTests/MemoryViewTests.swift (XCTest, @testable import Engram), three tests driven through the REAL EngramServiceClient over RecordingServiceTransport (the harness MemoryView actually binds the concrete client, so injecting a mock into the SwiftUI view is not the contract) plus the two extracted pure static helpers:
1. testInsightsCommandRoundTrips — EngramServiceClient over RecordingServiceTransport answering command \"insights\" with #\"[{\"id\":\"i1\",\"content\":\"a long enough insight body\",\"wing\":\"eng\",\"room\":null,\"importance\":7,\"created_at\":\"2026-06-01T00:00:00Z\"}]\"#; assert client.insights() decodes one EngramServiceInsightInfo with id==\"i1\", importance==7, and createdAt==\"2026-06-01T00:00:00Z\" (verifies the created_at CodingKey mapping).
2. testMemoryFileOptionalContentAndDetailFallback — JSONDecoder().decode an EngramServiceMemoryFile WITH a content field (assert MemoryView.detailText(for:) == full content) and one WITHOUT content (assert .content == nil and MemoryView.detailText(for:) == preview).
3. testInsightContentValidation — assert MemoryView.insightContentIsValid(\"too short\") == false (<10 trimmed) and insightContentIsValid(\"this is definitely long enough\") == true; include a whitespace-padded short string to confirm trimming.
Add a service-side test (under WP06-SVC's test ownership) asserting SQLiteEngramServiceReadProvider.insights() returns [] when the insights table is absent (fresh DB), mirroring existing embeddingStatus table-absent coverage; if WP06-SVC has no dedicated test file, fold this into the existing read-provider test target.
Run: xcodebuild -project macos/Engram.xcodeproj -scheme Engram -configuration Debug test.
- **Risks:** Primary risk is the serialization of WP06-SVC across four other WPs' files (WP16 Models, WP05+WP13 ReadProvider, WP14 CommandHandler). If those WPs reflow the same regions, WP06-SVC must rebase its additive hunks (all additions: one struct + one optional field; one protocol method + three conformer impls + one initializer arg; one dispatch case) — low textual-conflict surface because nothing existing is modified, only appended. Second risk: if WP06 lands its UI before WP06-SVC's API exists, MemoryView won't compile — mitigated by declaring WP06 dependent on WP06-SVC (UI is the last step). Third: the importance column is INTEGER in SQLite but EngramServiceInsightInfo.importance is Int — GRDB Row subscript to Int is exact, and the DEFAULT 5 covers NULL via `?? 5` in the mapping. content optionality is verified against the live testStage3 payload, so no regression there.
- **Out of scope:** Does NOT implement embeddings/semantic memory (memory_insights vector table) — CLAUDE.md states sqlite-vec is not implemented; insights are read text-only from the `insights` table. Does NOT add editing of an existing insight (only create + delete, matching the saveInsight/deleteInsight API). Does NOT add Reveal-in-Finder / open-in-editor for .md files (the full-content viewer closes memory-insights-3). Does NOT expose wing/room as user-editable taxonomy in the New Insight sheet — only importance is editable; wing/room default to nil. Does NOT change MCP get_insights (cost-insights) behavior. Does NOT touch favorites/hide/rename surfaces (other WPs). Deliberately does NOT have WP06 edit EngramServiceModels.swift (WP16), EngramServiceReadProvider.swift (WP05/WP13), or EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift (WP14) directly — those edits are owned by the serialized WP06-SVC item, which is the explicit ownership/serialization decision the critique required. sourceSessionId was intentionally cut from EngramServiceInsightInfo because the detail pane has no meaningful render for a raw session id; re-add only if a future WP introduces a 'jump to source session' affordance.

### WP07 — Agents page rebuild: grouping + confirm/dismiss + pending-suggestions inbox + manual Set-parent UI (inbox rows only) + live refresh

- **Disposition:** wire-up  ·  **Critique:** needs-revision (revised)
- **Closes:** agents-grouping-1, agents-grouping-2, agents-grouping-3, xc-deadends-4, xc-capability-matrix-6 (setParentSession limb only; linkSessions limb deferred — see outOfScopeNotes), xc-events-nav-2
- **Goal:** Turn AgentsView from a flat read-only SessionCard list into the real management surface for agent/parent-child grouping: list top-level parents with ExpandableSessionCard (disclosure + confirm/dismiss wired to the existing service client), add a flat "Pending suggestions" inbox so the Layer-2 heuristic is discoverable and actionable, add a "Set parent…" picker ON THE INBOX ROWS that calls the existing setParentSession capability (the documented Layer-3 manual link that today has zero UI), and make the page live-refresh as indexing adds sessions. Set-parent is delivered ONLY on AgentsView-owned pending-suggestion rows; it is NOT added to the grouping ExpandableSessionCards (that would require editing WP01's file).
- **Approach:** The backend is fully present; this is pure wire-up plus one tiny new read query and one new small picker component. Five concrete moves:

1) GROUPING (agents-grouping-1): Replace `SessionCard(session:){...}` with `ExpandableSessionCard(...)`, mirroring SessionsPageView. The card already exposes onTap/onChildTap/onConfirmSuggestion/onDismissSuggestion and loads its own children on expand (verified ExpandableSessionCard.swift:23-35, 241-262). AgentsView will list TOP-LEVEL PARENT sessions that actually have agent children, not the subagent sessions themselves. The current `db.listSessions(subAgent: true, limit: 200)` returns the children — wrong altitude for a grouping page. New load: list top-level sessions (`subAgent: false, topLevelOnly: true`), compute `childCount`/`suggestedChildCount` per id (db.childCount / db.suggestedChildCount), and keep only parents whose `confirmed+suggested > 0` so the page shows real groups, not every session. Wire confirm/dismiss to the same helpers SessionsPageView uses (serviceClient.confirmSuggestion / serviceClient.dismissSuggestion), then reload. I do NOT pass any per-card Set-parent closure — ExpandableSessionCard has no such parameter (verified: its only context-menu actions are Resume/Copy/Handoff/Replay at ExpandableSessionCard.swift:116-129; zero onSetParent symbol). Adding one would edit WP01's file. Cut.

2) PENDING-SUGGESTIONS INBOX (agents-grouping-2; satisfies the discoverability + actionability of the setParentSession limb of xc-capability-matrix-6): Add a "Pending suggestions" section above the groups that lists every session with a non-null suggested_parent_id awaiting review, with inline Confirm/Dismiss AND the Set-parent affordance. No existing DB method returns this flat list — `suggestedChildSessions(parentId:)` requires a known parent. Add ONE small read method `pendingSuggestionSessions(includeHidden:limit:)` to macos/Engram/Core/Database.swift, mirroring the existing suggestedChildSessions read (Database.swift:1091-1102) but without the parentId filter and with a LIMIT: a readInBackground query `SELECT * FROM sessions WHERE suggested_parent_id IS NOT NULL AND parent_session_id IS NULL [AND hidden_at IS NULL] ORDER BY start_time DESC LIMIT ?`. This is a read-only addition next to the existing method — allowed (read, nonisolated via readInBackground, not a writer). OWNERSHIP NOTE: Database.swift is shared and not in WP07's owned-files map; this WP explicitly claims a scoped grant to add ONLY this one read method (no writer, no edits to existing methods) — see risks. Each row gets Confirm (serviceClient.confirmSuggestion(sessionId:)) and Dismiss (guarded: `if let sp = child.suggestedParentId { serviceClient.dismissSuggestion(sessionId:, suggestedParentId: sp) }`).

3) MANUAL SET-PARENT, INBOX-ROWS-ONLY (agents-grouping-3, xc-deadends-4, setParentSession limb of xc-capability-matrix-6): Add a new component file macos/Engram/Views/Agents/LinkParentPicker.swift — a small sheet that takes a child Session, fetches candidate top-level parents via db.listSessions(subAgent:false, topLevelOnly:true, limit:200) off-main, lets the user search/select one, and on confirm calls serviceClient.setParentSession(sessionId: child.id, parentId: selected.id) (returns EngramServiceLinkResponse{ok,error}). AgentsView exposes a "Set parent…" affordance (overflow/context menu) ON EACH PENDING-SUGGESTION ROW (an AgentsView-owned row) that opens this sheet. On success: dismiss sheet + reload. I do NOT add a per-grouping-card Set-parent affordance (would edit WP01's ExpandableSessionCard). The inbox-row Set-parent fully closes agents-grouping-3 / xc-deadends-4 / the setParentSession half of xc-capability-matrix-6. CORRECTION TO WP BRIEF: linkSessions is NOT a session→parent link — EngramServiceLinkSessionsRequest carries `targetDir`/`actor` and re-associates sessions to a project DIRECTORY (returns created/skipped/projectNames), not a parent/child link. The manual parent link is setParentSession only. linkSessions is therefore out of scope for this WP (documented in outOfScopeNotes); I do NOT wire it.

4) LIVE REFRESH (xc-events-nav-2): Add `@Environment(EngramServiceStatusStore.self) var serviceStatusStore` and change `.task { await loadData() }` to `.task(id: serviceStatusStore.totalSessions) { await loadData() }`, matching ProjectsView/HomeView. serviceStatusStore.totalSessions exists and the store is injected app-wide.

5) Add `@Environment(EngramServiceClient.self) var serviceClient` (matches SessionsPageView) so confirm/dismiss/setParentSession are callable.
