- **UX behavior:** Hooks page:\n- Loading: on first open (and on refresh) while hooks is empty, a centered ProgressView shows instead of a blank scroll area. Once data arrives, sections render. If hooks already has data, refresh does NOT blank the page (spinner only when empty), avoiding flicker.\n- Empty: unchanged EmptyState ('No hooks configured') still shows only when !isLoading && hooks.isEmpty.\n- Error: unchanged AlertBanner at top.\n- Per-row actions: right-click a hook row -> 'Reveal in Finder' (opens Finder with the defining settings.json selected) and 'Open Settings File' (opens settings.json in the user's default editor). Both operate on the hook's own source file (global -> ~/.claude/settings.json, project -> ~/.claude/settings.local.json). This is the 'jump to hook' affordance.\n- Refresh: a header refresh Button and pull-to-refresh (.refreshable) both re-run loadData(); button is disabled while isLoading. After editing settings.json externally and refreshing, the new hooks appear.\n\nSkills page:\n- Loading: ProgressView when isLoading && skills.isEmpty (previously the page showed only the search box with no feedback during the recursive ~/.claude/plugins/cache scan).\n- Empty/Error/Search: unchanged.\n- Per-row action: right-click a skill row -> 'Reveal in Finder' selecting the skill's source file (.md for plugin skills, settings.json for global commands). Whole row is a tap/menu target via .contentShape.\n- Refresh: refresh Button + .refreshable re-run loadData().\n\nCross-page note: xc-events-nav-4 also names MemoryView. MemoryView is WP06-owned and is NOT touched here; the finding is only fully closed once WP06 adds the same refresh affordance to MemoryView. WP16 closes the Skills+Hooks portion.\n\nEdge cases:\n- Missing/relocated file: NSWorkspace.shared.selectFile and .open silently no-op if the path doesn't exist (acceptable — matches existing SourcePulseView/RepoDetailView behavior; no crash).\n- Tilde expansion: paths are ~-expanded display strings; helpers call NSString(string:).expandingTildeInPath before selectFile/open so the absolute path is used.\n- Service busy/unreachable: loadData already catches and sets `error`; the AlertBanner shows; refresh can be retried.\n- Empty-path hook: impossible post-fix (the single producer always populates path), so no guard code is added.
- **Acceptance:**
  - EngramServiceHookInfo has a non-optional `path: String` field; EngramServiceModels.swift compiles and the synthetic id remains scope/event/command.
  - FileSystemEngramServiceReadProvider.hooks() populates path with displayPath(url) for both global and project scopes (line 205); no other producer is changed. This single line lands via WP16's scoped exception OR is reassigned to the provider-owning WP (WP05/WP13) — the chosen resolution is recorded before implementation.
  - HooksView hookRow exposes a context menu with 'Reveal in Finder' and 'Open Settings File' operating on the hook's source settings.json via NSWorkspace selectFile/open after tilde expansion; whole row is the menu target via .contentShape.
  - SkillsView skillRow exposes a 'Reveal in Finder' context-menu item selecting the skill's source file via NSWorkspace.selectFile after tilde expansion.
  - Both pages render a ProgressView while isLoading && list is empty, and provide a working refresh (header Button + .refreshable) that re-runs loadData(); the button is disabled while isLoading.
  - New EngramTests/HooksSkillsTests.swift passes, asserting the hook DTO carries/decodes path and the reveal tilde-expansion contract holds.
  - The provider-side assertion (FileSystemEngramServiceReadProvider(homeDirectory:).hooks() returns a non-empty path for a settings.json fixture) is scheduled into the provider WP's work in EngramServiceCoreTests/EngramServiceIPCTests.swift (not WP16-owned) — flagged so the structural fix does not ship without producer-side coverage.
  - Engram app target builds (xcodebuild) and EngramTests + EngramServiceCoreTests pass.
  - xc-events-nav-4 is recorded as PARTIALLY closed by WP16 (Skills+Hooks); MemoryView refresh remains WP06's responsibility for full closure.
- **Test plan:** Owned test file macos/EngramTests/HooksSkillsTests.swift (target EngramTests, @testable import Engram):\n1. testHookInfoCarriesAndDecodesPath: build EngramServiceHookInfo(event:\"PostToolUse\", command:\"echo hi\", scope:\"global\", path:\"~/.claude/settings.json\"), encode+decode via JSONEncoder/JSONDecoder, assert decoded.path == original and decoded.id == \"global/PostToolUse/echo hi\".\n2. testHookInfoDecodesServiceJSONWithPath: decode literal Data for {\"event\":\"...\",\"command\":\"...\",\"scope\":\"project\",\"path\":\"~/.claude/settings.local.json\"} and assert .path.\n3. testRevealPathExpandsTilde: assert NSString(string:\"~/.claude/settings.json\").expandingTildeInPath does not contain \"~\" and hasPrefix(\"/\").\nThese cover the DTO field this WP adds and the reveal helper's expansion contract (the only added logic that is unit-testable without UI/AppKit window interaction).\n\nProvider-side coverage (NOT owned by WP16, must be SCHEDULED into the provider WP): add a test in macos/EngramServiceCoreTests/EngramServiceIPCTests.swift — the only target that can see the provider — alongside the existing `FileSystemEngramServiceReadProvider(homeDirectory: root)` usage (line 2631) and the existing `client.hooks()` call (line 1181). The test writes a settings.json fixture with a `hooks` block under `root`, calls `FileSystemEngramServiceReadProvider(homeDirectory: root).hooks()` (provider init at EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:94-98), and asserts the returned hook's `path` is non-empty and resolves under `root`. This is the only test that verifies hooks() actually EMITS the path; the three owned DTO/expansion tests do not. This requirement is flagged here rather than silently skipped because the test file is not WP16-owned.\n\nContext-menu/reveal/refresh are SwiftUI+AppKit side effects (NSWorkspace), not unit-testable here; verified manually per acceptance criteria.
- **Risks:** Low-to-moderate, dominated by one ownership-boundary item.\n\n(1) OWNERSHIP CONFLICT (blocking until resolved): the producer-side populate (line 205 in EngramServiceReadProvider.swift) lands in a file owned by WP05 (replayTimeline) and WP13 (source-status), not WP16. RESOLUTION: WP16 requests a SCOPED EXCEPTION limited to the disjoint hooks() block (195-210); the change is a single argument added to one initializer and does not touch replayTimeline (212/630) or source-status, so a clean 3-way merge is expected. If the exception is denied, the one-line populate is reassigned to whichever WP lands the provider file (WP05 or WP13), and WP16 proceeds with its DTO + view + test work unblocked (the DTO field already makes `path` available; only its population moves owners). The chosen resolution must be recorded in the orchestrator's ownership map before implementation. NOTE: the original spec only flagged the provider-side TEST as foreign; this revision also flags the provider-side PRODUCTION edit.\n\n(2) Codable change: adding a non-optional `path` to EngramServiceHookInfo is safe because hook data is recomputed from settings.json on every call (never persisted) and the only encoder is EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:80 re-encoding the same provider output — so every emitted JSON will carry path. The sole constructor is line 205 (grep: one match); SQLite delegates (626), Empty returns [] (49). The one known test call site (EngramServiceIPCTests.swift:1181) consumes client.hooks() and does NOT construct the DTO, so it does not need updating. If any future test constructs the DTO without path it will fail to compile (compile-time caught, not a runtime decode break).\n\n(3) selectFile/open are fire-and-forget AppKit calls with no failure surface; missing files no-op silently, matching existing SourcePulseView/RepoDetailView behavior.\n\n(4) Provider-side coverage gap: the three owned unit tests do NOT prove hooks() emits a non-empty path; that assertion must be scheduled into the provider WP (see testPlan). If it is not, the structural fix ships without producer coverage — flagged, not silently skipped.
- **Out of scope:** - Does NOT fully close xc-events-nav-4: that finding names MemoryView + SkillsView + HooksView. WP16 adds refresh to Skills and Hooks only. MemoryView.swift is WP06-owned and is NOT touched here; full closure requires WP06 to add the same .refreshable/refresh affordance to MemoryView. xc-events-nav-4 is therefore recorded as PARTIAL under WP16, with the Memory facet a cross-WP dependency on WP06.\n- Does NOT make the producer-side edit under WP16's default ownership: EngramServiceReadProvider.swift is WP05/WP13-owned. The one-line hooks() populate ships only via an explicit scoped exception or by reassignment to the provider-owning WP (see Risks). WP16 does NOT touch replayTimeline, source-status, or any other part of that file.\n- Does NOT add the provider-side unit test into EngramServiceCoreTests itself (not an owned file) — only flags it as required work for the provider WP.\n- Does NOT add enable/disable/test/toggle/run-hook or run-skill actions — there is no backend mutation command (grep for disableHook/testHook/enableHook returns zero) and running a skill is a Claude Code harness action the app cannot invoke; building that backend is out of this wire-up WP's scope.\n- Does NOT add file-watch/auto-reload (only manual refresh + .refreshable, per the findings' lowest-effort suggestion).\n- Does NOT surface hook matcher/type structure (hookCommands flattens them; the findings flag matcher/type as optional, not required for jump-to-hook).\n- Does NOT change the synthetic hook id (stays scope/event/command).\n- Does NOT add a defensive empty-path branch — empty path is impossible post-fix (single producer always populates).\n- Keeps two context-menu items on Hooks (Reveal + Open) because hooks-config-1 explicitly names both 'open the settings.json' and 'reveal it in Finder'; this is the finding's minimum, not scope creep. Skills gets the single Reveal item it asks for.

### WP17 — Observability honesty: remove Performance+Traces, fix log reader/warn/redaction, gate the surface, and repair the now-red UITests

- **Disposition:** mixed  ·  **Critique:** needs-revision (revised)
- **Closes:** observability-1, observability-2, observability-3, observability-4, observability-5, observability-6, xc-deadends-6
- **Goal:** Make the Observability surface honest: delete the two permanently-empty tabs (Performance, Traces), make the log/error reader actually show message text (un-redact both interpolation paths) and stop offering a dead 'warn' filter, document the Health tab's real signal and the inert health() stub, gate the whole developer-diagnostics surface behind a 'Show Developer Tools' flag, and repair the unowned UITest target (ObservabilityTests + ObservabilityScreen + TestLaunchConfig) that the tab removal and default-off gate would otherwise turn red.
- **Approach:** Five honest, surgical changes plus one mandatory UITest repair the original spec missed.

(1) REMOVE Performance + Traces tabs [observability-1, xc-deadends-6]. Both panels are static EmptyState with zero data source — confirmed: no os_signpost/recordSpan/recordMetric writer exists; the traces/metrics tables only get CREATEd in migrations; Database.swift's fetchTraces/slowTraces/recentHourlyMetrics (which touch TraceEntry/HourlyMetric) have zero callers. Real span/metric instrumentation is DEFERRED (out of scope). Fix: drop `.performance` and `.traces` from `ObservabilityView.Tab`, drop their `switch` arms. Delete PerformanceView.swift (orphan I created). In TraceExplorerView.swift delete ONLY the `TraceExplorerView` struct + its OBS-C1 header; KEEP `StatusBadge`, `TraceEntry`, `HourlyMetric` because Database.swift (out of scope) still references TraceEntry/HourlyMetric — deleting them breaks a file this WP does not own. Those are pre-existing dead code: flag, do not delete. xcodegen is directory-based so the filename is irrelevant.

(2) UN-REDACT log bodies [observability-3]. EngramLogger.info/warn/error/debug interpolate the message with privacy:.private, so a non-entitled OSLogStore read returns '<private>'. These are developer diagnostic strings, not user PII. Flip to privacy:.public on ALL FOUR methods. CRITICAL per critique: info/warn/debug interpolate `\(message, ...)` but error() interpolates a COMPUTED `\(msg, ...)` (line 33, `msg = error.map {...} ?? message`). The implementer must flip the `msg` interpolation in error() too — flipping only `message` leaves the error path redacted. `\(msg, privacy: .public)` on a non-literal String is valid Swift/OSLog; verify all four build.

(3) DROP the dead 'warn' filter [observability-4]. macOS unified logging stores os_log .warning at the .error log type; OSLogReader.levelString maps that to 'error' and never returns 'warn' (OSLogReaderTests line 27 already asserts `case .error: return "warn"` is absent). So the 'warn' picker option always yields 0 rows and real warnings inflate the error count. Honest fix: remove 'warn' from LogStreamView.levels (line 15 → ["All","debug","info","error"]) and remove the `case "warn": return .orange` branch from LevelBadge (lines 162-163). Leave OSLogReader's error/fault→error mapping as-is (correct). Document in Error+Health copy that the 24h count includes warning-level entries so the KPI is not silently overstated.

(4) HEALTH stub honesty [observability-5]. health() returns a hardcoded 'healthy' literal across all three read providers and has ZERO callers app-wide (confirmed: grep '.health()' across Engram/ + Shared/ = 0). SystemHealthView already derives real signal from serviceStatusStore + DB pragmas + OSLogReader. Disposition: remove-misleading, but the stub lives in EngramServiceReadProvider.swift (owned by WP05/WP13, NOT this WP). In-scope: add a doc note in SystemHealthView that Health is DB-pragma + service-status + unified-log only and intentionally does NOT call the constant health() stub. Do NOT build a real health() payload (backend change, DEFERRED).

(5) GATE the surface [observability-6]. Add `@AppStorage("showDeveloperTools") var showDeveloperTools = false` to ObservabilityView. When false it renders an EmptyState pointing to Settings > General; when true it renders the picker+tabs. This in-view gate is the SAFETY NET. The sidebar item + route gating (Screen.swift/SidebarView.swift — WP02) and the Settings toggle (GeneralSettingsSection.swift — WP12) are the primary UX and are NOT owned here. They are declared as a hard merge precondition (see risks), because the EmptyState copy tells the user to enable a toggle that does not exist until WP12 lands and the sidebar item stays visible until WP02 lands.

(6) REPAIR the now-red UITests [BLOCKER from critique — missing in original]. macos/EngramUITests/Tests/FullTests/ObservabilityTests.swift and macos/EngramUITests/Screens/ObservabilityScreen.swift are NOT in any WP's owned set, but tab removal + the default-OFF gate make ALL FIVE existing UITests fail on a default build: testTraceExplorer/testPerformanceCharts select tabs that no longer exist; testLogStream/testErrorDashboard/testSystemHealth fail because the gate renders an EmptyState with no tab container. This WP must own and fix them or it ships a guaranteed-red target. Fix: (a) delete testTraceExplorer + testPerformanceCharts; (b) in ObservabilityScreen.swift set `tabs = ["Logs","Errors","Health"]` and delete the `performance` + `traceExplorer` element accessors; (c) add `-showDeveloperTools YES` to TestLaunchConfig.mainWindow's launchArguments so the gate does not swallow the container — passing it as an NSUserDefaults argument-domain pair means @AppStorage("showDeveloperTools") reads true automatically, no AppEnvironment parsing needed.

observability-2 RE-SCOPED honestly per critique: the privacy flip (3) un-redacts message bodies app-side, but observability-2's CORE claim — the app's currentProcess OSLogStore cannot see com.engram.service entries cross-process at all — is NOT closed by this WP. Scope of observability-2 here = (i) mirror the ServiceLogger.swift privacy:.private→.public flip (flagged companion edit, file unowned), and (ii) document the cross-process limitation in SystemHealthView. The real fix (EngramService persisting a readable log ring read via IPC) is a backend build and is DEFERRED.
- **Changes:**
  - `edit` `macos/Engram/Views/Pages/ObservabilityView.swift` — Remove .performance and .traces from the Tab enum and their two switch arms (leaving logs/errors/health). Add @AppStorage("showDeveloperTools") var showDeveloperTools = false. Wrap body: when showDeveloperTools is false render an EmptyState(icon:"wrench.and.screwdriver", title:"Developer diagnostics hidden", message:"Observability shows internal logs and health. Enable Settings > General > Show Developer Tools to view it.") still tagged accessibilityIdentifier("observability_container"); when true render the existing picker+tabs (also tagged observability_container). Fix initial @State selectedTab default stays .logs.
  - `edit` `macos/Engram/Views/Observability/PerformanceView.swift` — Delete the file (PerformanceView struct is orphaned by removing the Performance tab; orphan this WP created).
  - `edit` `macos/Engram/Views/Observability/TraceExplorerView.swift` — Delete the TraceExplorerView struct and its OBS-C1 doc comment. KEEP StatusBadge, TraceEntry, HourlyMetric (consumed by Database.swift fetchTraces/slowTraces/recentHourlyMetrics, out of scope). Add a one-line comment that these survive only for the unused Database trace/metric read methods (pre-existing dead code, flagged not deleted).
  - `edit` `macos/Engram/Views/Observability/LogStreamView.swift` — Remove 'warn' from the levels array (line 15) → ["All", "debug", "info", "error"]. Remove the `case "warn": return .orange` branch from LevelBadge (lines 162-163).
  - `edit` `macos/Engram/Views/Observability/ErrorDashboardView.swift` — Add a clarifying caption under the 'Errors (24h)' KPI: a single Text line noting the count includes warning-level entries because the unified log stores warnings at the error type. No logic change.
  - `edit` `macos/Engram/Views/Observability/SystemHealthView.swift` — Update the 'Recent Errors' caption (line 50 area) to note the count includes warning-level entries (unified-log limitation). Add a one-line doc comment that Health is DB-pragma + service-status + unified-log only and intentionally does NOT call the constant health() IPC stub, and that cross-process com.engram.service log entries are not readable from the app process (observability-2, deferred).
  - `edit` `macos/Engram/Core/EngramLogger.swift` — Change privacy:.private → privacy:.public on all four methods: info `\(message, privacy: .public)`, warn `\(message, privacy: .public)`, debug `\(message, privacy: .public)`, and error `\(msg, privacy: .public)` (line 33 — flip the COMPUTED msg interpolation, not just `message`). No remaining `privacy: .private` in this file.
  - `edit` `macos/EngramUITests/Tests/FullTests/ObservabilityTests.swift` — Delete testTraceExplorer and testPerformanceCharts (their tabs no longer exist). Keep testLogStream/testErrorDashboard/testSystemHealth — they pass once -showDeveloperTools YES (added to TestLaunchConfig.mainWindow) keeps the tab container rendered. No other change needed; navigateToObservability + selectTab still valid for the three surviving tabs.
  - `edit` `macos/EngramUITests/Screens/ObservabilityScreen.swift` — Change static tabs (line 27) to ["Logs","Errors","Health"]. Delete the `performance` and `traceExplorer` element accessors (lines 15-16). Leave container/tabPicker/logStream/errorDashboard/health and selectTab unchanged.
  - `edit` `macos/EngramUITests/Helpers/TestLaunchConfig.swift` — In configure(_:) for the .mainWindow case, append ["-showDeveloperTools", "YES"] to launchArguments so the default-OFF gate does not render the EmptyState and swallow observability_container during UI tests (NSUserDefaults argument-domain pair → @AppStorage("showDeveloperTools") reads true automatically).
  - `create` `macos/EngramTests/ObservabilityTests.swift` — New XCTest (EngramTests target, @testable import Engram). Source-assert: ObservabilityView.swift has no 'case performance'/'case traces'/'PerformanceView()'/'TraceExplorerView()' and references @AppStorage("showDeveloperTools"); LogStreamView.swift levels line has no '\"warn\"' and LevelBadge has no 'case \"warn\"'; EngramLogger.swift contains 'privacy: .public' and NOT 'privacy: .private'. Plus behavioral: EngramLogger.warn(token); poll OSLogReader.recentLogs(hours:1) and assert an entry containing the token exists and is not '<private>' (XCTSkip on OSLogReaderError, mirroring OSLogReaderTests' env guard). Note: class name collides with the EngramUITests ObservabilityTests but they are in SEPARATE targets — no symbol collision, intentional.
- **APIs used:**
  - `OSLogReader.recentLogs(level:module:hours:limit:)` (macos/Engram/Core/OSLogReader.swift) `static func recentLogs(level: String = "All", module: String = "All", hours: Double = 24, limit: Int = 200) throws -> LogQueryResult` ✓
  - `OSLogReader.countErrors(hours:)` (macos/Engram/Core/OSLogReader.swift) `static func countErrors(hours: Double = 24) throws -> Int` ✓
  - `OSLogReader.levelString` (macos/Engram/Core/OSLogReader.swift) `private static func levelString(_ level: OSLogEntryLog.Level) -> String  // maps to debug/info/error only; OSLogReaderTests line 27 asserts no .error→"warn" mapping` ✓
  - `EngramLogger.info/warn/debug` (macos/Engram/Core/EngramLogger.swift) `static func info/warn/debug(_ message: String, module: LogModule)  // currently logger.<level>("\(message, privacy: .private)") → flip to .public` ✓
  - `EngramLogger.error` (macos/Engram/Core/EngramLogger.swift) `static func error(_ message: String, module: LogModule, error: Error? = nil)  // line 32 `let msg = error.map {...} ?? message`; line 33 logs "\(msg, privacy: .private)" → flip the COMPUTED msg interpolation to .public` ✓
  - `ServiceLogger.warn/info/debug/notice/error` (macos/EngramService/Core/ServiceLogger.swift) `public static func warn(_ message: String, category: ServiceLogCategory)  // logger.<level>("\(message, privacy: .private)") — NOT owned, flagged mirror edit for observability-2 service half` ✓
  - `EngramServiceReadProvider.health()` (macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceReadProvider.swift) `func health() async throws -> EngramServiceHealthResponse  // returns hardcoded ok:true status:'healthy' in all impls; ZERO app callers (grep '.health()' across Engram/+Shared/ = 0) — NOT owned, do not build` ✓
  - `ObservabilityView.Tab` (macos/Engram/Views/Pages/ObservabilityView.swift) `enum Tab: String, CaseIterable { case logs="Logs", errors="Errors", performance="Performance", traces="Traces", health="Health" }  // remove performance + traces; @State selectedTab default .logs` ✓
  - `EmptyState` (macos/Engram/Components/EmptyState.swift) `struct EmptyState: View { let icon: String; let title: String; let message: String; ... }` ✓
  - `TraceEntry / HourlyMetric / StatusBadge` (macos/Engram/Views/Observability/TraceExplorerView.swift) `struct TraceEntry; struct HourlyMetric; struct StatusBadge  // TraceEntry/HourlyMetric consumed by Database.swift (0 callers) — keep all, pre-existing dead` ✓
  - `Database.fetchTraces/slowTraces/recentHourlyMetrics` (macos/Engram/Core/Database.swift) `func fetchTraces(nameFilter:limit:)->[TraceEntry]; slowTraces(minDurationMs:limit:)->[TraceEntry]; recentHourlyMetrics(limit:)->[HourlyMetric]  // zero callers; reason TraceEntry/HourlyMetric must survive deletion` ✓
  - `@AppStorage showDockIcon (pattern ref)` (macos/Engram/Views/Settings/GeneralSettingsSection.swift) `@AppStorage("showDockIcon") var showDockIcon: Bool = false (line 7); UserDefaults.standard.bool(forKey: "showDockIcon") in MenuBarController (lines 307/434) — model for the new showDeveloperTools flag` ✓
  - `TestLaunchConfig.configure / .mainWindow` (macos/EngramUITests/Helpers/TestLaunchConfig.swift) `func configure(_ app: XCUIApplication) { app.launchArguments += [...]; case .mainWindow: app.launchArguments += ["--window-size",...] }  // append ["-showDeveloperTools","YES"] in .mainWindow` ✓
  - `ObservabilityScreen (UITest page object)` (macos/EngramUITests/Screens/ObservabilityScreen.swift) `static let tabs = ["Logs","Errors","Performance","Traces","Health"] (line 27); var performance/traceExplorer element accessors (lines 15-16) — update tabs to 3, delete the two accessors` ✓
  - `EngramUITests ObservabilityTests` (macos/EngramUITests/Tests/FullTests/ObservabilityTests.swift) `func testLogStream/testTraceExplorer/testErrorDashboard/testPerformanceCharts/testSystemHealth — delete testTraceExplorer + testPerformanceCharts (removed tabs); others pass once gate is opened via launch arg` ✓
- **UX behavior:** Tabs: Observability shows a 3-segment picker (Logs, Errors, Health) instead of 5. No user can land on a permanently-empty Performance/Traces panel.

Gating: With 'Show Developer Tools' OFF (default), opening Observability (if reachable) shows an EmptyState: icon 'wrench.and.screwdriver', title 'Developer diagnostics hidden', message 'Observability shows internal logs and health. Enable Settings > General > Show Developer Tools to view it.' The companion WP02 sidebar edit hides the sidebar item entirely when OFF, so the common path is the item simply not appearing; the companion WP12 edit adds the Settings toggle the message points to. With the flag ON, the full tabbed surface appears.

Logs tab: Level picker offers All/debug/info/error (no 'warn'). Loading shows ProgressView('Loading logs...'); on OSLogReaderError shows the existing AlertBanner('System log not available under current permissions.'); empty shows 'No log entries'. Message column now renders real text instead of '<private>'. Warnings emitted by the code appear under the 'error' filter (unified-log limitation) — now documented.

Errors tab: 'Errors (24h)' KPI unchanged in computation but gains a caption noting it includes warning-level entries (the unified log cannot separate warnings from errors). OSLogReaderError still surfaces the existing 'not available' AlertBanner; other failures still surface 'Failed to load errors: ...'. Recent-error message text is now readable (un-redacted, including the error() path).

Health tab: unchanged real signal (DB size/file, journal mode, index-scan status from serviceStatusStore, 24h error count). Recent-Errors caption updated to note it counts warning+error entries. A code comment documents Health does not call the inert health() IPC and that cross-process service logs are not app-readable. When OSLogStore is inaccessible it still says 'System log not available...' rather than a false all-clear.

UITests: with -showDeveloperTools YES in TestLaunchConfig.mainWindow, the gate is open during tests so observability_container and the tabs render; the three surviving UI tests (Logs/Errors/Health) pass; the two removed-tab tests are deleted.

Edge cases: OSLogStore denied → 'not available' banners (already handled). Service stopped/starting → index-scan StatusRow reflects it (already handled). Flag toggled while Observability is open → @AppStorage is observed, view re-renders to/from the gated EmptyState immediately.
- **Acceptance:**
  - ObservabilityView.Tab has exactly logs/errors/health; PerformanceView and TraceExplorerView structs are no longer referenced anywhere in Engram/.
  - PerformanceView.swift is deleted; TraceExplorerView.swift retains StatusBadge/TraceEntry/HourlyMetric (so Database.swift still compiles) but no longer defines TraceExplorerView.
  - LogStreamView.levels does not contain 'warn'; LevelBadge has no warn→orange branch.
  - EngramLogger info/warn/error/debug interpolate the message with privacy:.public (no remaining privacy:.private), including the error() method's computed `msg` interpolation.
  - ObservabilityView gates its tabbed content behind @AppStorage('showDeveloperTools'); with the flag false it shows the 'Developer diagnostics hidden' EmptyState; observability_container identifier is present in both states.
  - Error and Health tabs display a caption noting the 24h error count includes warning-level entries.
  - EngramUITests ObservabilityTests no longer has testTraceExplorer/testPerformanceCharts; ObservabilityScreen.tabs == ['Logs','Errors','Health'] with no performance/traceExplorer accessors; TestLaunchConfig.mainWindow passes -showDeveloperTools YES.
  - New macos/EngramTests/ObservabilityTests.swift passes; existing OSLogReaderTests still passes (its 'never returns warn' assertion remains valid).
  - xcodebuild Debug succeeds; the EngramUITests target compiles and its surviving Observability UI tests pass on a default build.
- **Test plan:** Add macos/EngramTests/ObservabilityTests.swift (XCTest, @testable import Engram), mirroring OSLogReaderTests' source-read style plus one behavioral check:
- testObservabilityTabsDropPerformanceAndTraces: read ObservabilityView.swift source; assert it does NOT contain 'case performance' / 'case traces' / 'PerformanceView()' / 'TraceExplorerView()'.
- testLogStreamHasNoWarnFilter: read LogStreamView.swift source; assert the levels line has no '\"warn\"' and LevelBadge has no 'case \"warn\"'.
- testEngramLoggerUsesPublicPrivacy: read EngramLogger.swift source; assert it contains 'privacy: .public' and NOT 'privacy: .private' (the NOT-.private half is load-bearing — it catches a forgotten error()/msg path even though one stray .public would satisfy the positive half).
- testObservabilityIsGated: read ObservabilityView.swift source; assert it references @AppStorage(\"showDeveloperTools\").
- testEmittedWarnMessageIsReadable (behavioral): EngramLogger.warn(token); poll OSLogReader.recentLogs(hours:1) and assert an entry whose message contains the token exists and is not '<private>' (XCTSkip on OSLogReaderError, matching OSLogReaderTests' environment guard).
UITest target is validated by the existing EngramUITests Observability suite after its repair: testLogStream/testErrorDashboard/testSystemHealth must still pass (gate opened via -showDeveloperTools YES); testTraceExplorer/testPerformanceCharts are removed. This satisfies the test-coverage rule for every behavior change (tab removal, warn-filter removal, privacy flip both paths, gating, UITest surface).
- **Risks:** HARD MERGE PRECONDITION (cross-WP gating dependency — must be sequenced, not just flagged): the in-ObservabilityView EmptyState tells the user to enable 'Settings > General > Show Developer Tools', a toggle that does NOT exist until WP12 edits GeneralSettingsSection.swift, and the sidebar item stays visible until WP02 edits Screen.swift + SidebarView.swift to hide it when showDeveloperTools is off. WP17 must NOT merge ahead of WP02 + WP12, or the default experience is: Observability still appears in the sidebar, opens to an EmptyState referencing a non-existent setting. The in-view gate is only the safety net; WP02 (sidebar/route) and WP12 (Settings toggle) are the primary UX and own those files.

Companion mirror edit (NOT in this WP's owned set): ServiceLogger.swift privacy:.private→.public on its 5 methods for the service half of observability-2/3. Owned via WP05/WP13's EngramServiceReadProvider, but ServiceLogger itself is unowned; without it com.engram.service messages stay redacted even when/if reachable.

observability-2 is only PARTIALLY closed here (re-scoped honestly): the app's currentProcess OSLogStore cannot read com.engram.service entries cross-process at all. This WP fixes only the redaction sub-part app-side and documents the cross-process gap. The real fix (EngramService persisting a readable log ring read via IPC) is a backend build and is DEFERRED. observability-5's health() remains a stub by design (documented, not built).

Class-name note (no action, reviewer awareness): the new macos/EngramTests/ObservabilityTests.swift and the existing macos/EngramUITests/.../ObservabilityTests.swift share the class name ObservabilityTests but live in separate targets (EngramTests vs EngramUITests) — no symbol collision, no overwrite.

Build risk: confirm `\(msg, privacy: .public)` (non-literal String interpolation in error()) compiles — it is valid Swift/OSLog; verify all four methods build in the xcodebuild Debug step.
- **Out of scope:** Does NOT build real Performance/Trace telemetry (no os_signpost span recording, no metric aggregation) — that is the DEFERRED backend work the empty tabs stood in for. Does NOT make health() return real signal — the stub is documented as unused, not implemented. Does NOT implement cross-process service-log reading (EngramService log ring / IPC error feed) — observability-2's root cause stays DEFERRED; only its redaction half is fixed app-side, with ServiceLogger flagged for a mirror edit. Does NOT delete Database.swift's dead fetchTraces/slowTraces/recentHourlyMetrics or the TraceEntry/HourlyMetric/StatusBadge types they consume — pre-existing dead code outside this WP, flagged for separate cleanup. Does NOT edit Screen.swift / SidebarView.swift (WP02), GeneralSettingsSection.swift (WP12), ServiceLogger.swift, or EngramServiceReadProvider.swift (WP05/WP13) — declared as sequenced companions / flagged mirrors. DOES now own the UITest repair (EngramUITests ObservabilityTests + ObservabilityScreen + TestLaunchConfig) that the original spec omitted, because tab removal and the default-off gate make that target red regardless of nominal file ownership.

### WP18 — Command palette completion + shared visual-token additions (cornerRadius + longLabel)

- **Disposition:** mixed  ·  **Critique:** needs-revision (revised)
- **Closes:** command-palette-1, command-palette-2, command-palette-3, command-palette-4, command-palette-6, xc-visual-3 (token only; call-site application handed to WP09/WP01), xc-visual-4 (token only; call-site application handed to WP12)
- **Goal:** Make the command palette a real action hub (global action commands + actionable session results), kill its dead model/state surface, keep keyboard selection on-screen, and ADD the two shared visual tokens (Theme.cornerRadius, SourceColors.longLabel) that the named card/banner/tier components and the Settings source-name table need to stop re-spelling values. WP18 OWNS adding the tokens; it does NOT apply them at call sites that live in other WPs' files — those applications are handed off to the owning WPs so xc-visual-2/3/4 actually close without WP18 reaching across ownership boundaries.
- **Approach:** Two clusters. The PALETTE cluster (sound and minimal, kept as-is per critique) is confined to PaletteItem.swift (WP18-sole), CommandPaletteView.swift (now WP18-sole — see ownership resolution below), and MainWindowView.swift (WP18-sole). The VISUAL-TOKEN cluster is scoped DOWN to ONLY adding the tokens in Theme.swift + SourceColors.swift (the two files WP18 owns); the call-site applications are NOT done here — they are spec'd as handoffs to the owning WPs so WP18 never edits another WP's file.\n\nOWNERSHIP RESOLUTION (critique blocker #1 — CommandPaletteView.swift double-owned with WP04):\nWP18 takes SOLE ownership of macos/Engram/Views/CommandPaletteView.swift. Rationale: WP18's change is the structural rewrite of this file — it replaces the inline `AnyPaletteRow` value type and the `visibleItems` mapping with real `.action`/`.session` PaletteItems, rewrites `filteredCommands`, and rewrites the key-handling block. WP04's search-mode work (debounce/query/SearchPageView) is a smaller delta that must build ON TOP of WP18's rewritten `visibleItems`/`sessionResults` surface, not race it. Resolution: WP04 is re-scoped to SearchPageView.swift ONLY for its standalone work; any CommandPaletteView.swift search-mode tweak WP04 needs is SEQUENCED AFTER WP18 merges (WP18 → then WP04 rebases its search-mode tweak on WP18's `sessionResults` shape). This removes the hard conflict: exactly one WP (WP18) edits CommandPaletteView.swift in this batch. If the orchestrator prefers WP04 as palette owner instead, the entire PALETTE cluster of this spec moves verbatim into WP04 — but it must be a SINGLE owner either way.\n\nPALETTE (model + view, surgical):\n1. command-palette-1/2 (wire-up): Add `PaletteItem.actionCommands(navigate:refreshUsage:regenerateTitles:)` factory in PaletteItem.swift producing `.action`-category items for the three REAL, session-less global actions with confirmed backends/nav: \"Open Settings\" (calls the passed `navigate(.settings)` — same channel MainWindowView already routes), \"Refresh Usage Data\" (`serviceClient.refreshUsage()` — confirmed real, used in SettingsView), \"Regenerate All Titles\" (`serviceClient.regenerateAllTitles()` — confirmed real, used in AISettingsSection). Deliberately DROP a Re-index/Refresh-Index command (NO reindex/forceReindex method exists; the only sync-shaped method `triggerSync` is a confirmed stub returning ok:false / \"Sync is not implemented in the Swift service\", so wiring it would be misleading) and DROP global Resume/Export (the palette has no current-session context; those belong on session rows — command-palette-4). CommandPaletteView's `filteredCommands` appends `actionCommands` to `navigationCommands` in command mode, filtered by the same title-contains predicate; `visibleItems` maps both through their existing `cmd.action` closures. Action closures that call async service methods wrap in `Task { try? await ... }` then `dismiss()` (mirrors AISettingsSection fire-and-forget pattern).\n2. command-palette-2 (wire-up, second half): Route session hits through a real `.session`-category PaletteItem instead of the inline `AnyPaletteRow`, so `.session` stops being a dead enum case. Add `PaletteItem.sessionResult(id:title:subtitle:onSelect:onResume:onExport:)` whose primary `action` navigates and whose `secondaryActions` are Resume + Export. Delete the now-orphaned `AnyPaletteRow` struct (orphan created by THIS change) and map `visibleItems` to `[PaletteItem]` directly.\n3. command-palette-4 (wire-up): Extend `PaletteItem` with `secondaryActions: [PaletteAction]` (default []) and a small `PaletteAction { id,label,icon,run }` value type. CommandPaletteView renders secondaryActions as trailing buttons that appear ONLY on the selected row, and binds Cmd-Return→first secondary (Resume), Opt-Return→second (Export) via the macOS-14-safe `.onKeyPress { keyPress in ... }` closure overload inspecting `keyPress.key == .return` + `keyPress.modifiers`. Export calls `serviceClient.exportSession(EngramServiceExportSessionRequest(id:hit.id, format:\"markdown\", outputHome:nil, actor:nil))` (confirmed signature) and shows a transient confirmation of the returned `outputPath`. Resume fetches the Session via the existing detached `db.getSession(id:)` path then sets `@State resumeSession`, presented via `.sheet` over the palette (ResumeDialog self-contains its service env + dismiss).\n4. command-palette-3 (remove-misleading): delete the dead `@State private var paletteItems` / `paletteSelection` lines (MainWindowView.swift:8-9) — verified zero reads/writes.\n5. command-palette-6 (wire-up): wrap the results `ScrollView`/`LazyVStack` in `ScrollViewReader` + `.onChange(of: selectedIndex) { proxy.scrollTo(visibleItems[selectedIndex].id, anchor: .center) }`, guarded against empty/out-of-range.\n\nVISUAL TOKENS — ADD ONLY (xc-visual-3, xc-visual-4):\n6. xc-visual-3 (token add only): add `static let cornerRadius: CGFloat = 8` to Theme.swift in a new `// MARK: - Layout` group (8 is the dominant existing value). WP18 does NOT apply it. The call-site application (KPICard.swift 10→token is WP09; SessionCard.swift / ExpandableSessionCard.swift 8→token is WP01/unowned) is HANDED OFF: WP09 and WP01 apply `Theme.cornerRadius` in their own files. Adding the unused token is a zero-risk, self-contained constant; it does not by itself change rendering.\n7. xc-visual-4 (token add only): add `static func longLabel(for:) -> String` to SourceColors.swift returning the disambiguated longer Settings names (\"Codex\",\"Claude Code\",\"OpenCode\",\"Copilot\",\"Gemini CLI\",\"iFlow\",\"Qwen\",\"Qoder\",\"Kimi\",\"Cline\"), falling back to `label(for:)` for unlisted ids. WP18 does NOT touch SettingsView. The repoint of `SettingsView.displayName(for:)` and the `defaultRows` literals at `SourceColors.longLabel` (killing the duplicate switch and the \"Iflow\"→\"iFlow\" fix) is HANDED OFF to WP12, which owns SettingsView.swift. All call-site applications for cornerRadius/longLabel are likewise removed from WP18's changes — WP18 ships the tokens, the owners ship the applications.
- **Changes:**

- **UX behavior:** PALETTE COMMAND MODE (type \">\"): list shows navigation rows (\"Go to ...\") PLUS three action rows: \"Open Settings\", \"Refresh Usage Data\", \"Regenerate All Titles\". Trailing-text filter matches action titles too. Open Settings → palette dismisses, window navigates to Settings. Refresh Usage Data → fires serviceClient.refreshUsage() in a Task, dismisses immediately (best-effort, failure silently swallowed, parity with SettingsView). Regenerate All Titles → fires regenerateAllTitles() in a Task, dismisses immediately. No spinner after dismiss (consistent with existing fire-and-forget settings actions).\n\nPALETTE SEARCH MODE (no \">\"): session results render as before, but the SELECTED row now shows two trailing buttons: play-glyph \"Resume\" and export-glyph \"Export\". Plain Return / click still navigates (onSelectSession) — unchanged default. Cmd-Return on the selected row → Resume: opens the existing ResumeDialog sheet over the palette (fetches Session by id off-main; nil → no-op, palette stays open). Opt-Return → Export: exportSession(format:\"markdown\"); success → transient single-line \"Exported to .../...md\" replaces the empty-results hint for ~2s; error → \"Export failed\". Buttons appear only on the selected row; arrowing moves which row exposes them.\n\nKEYBOARD SCROLL (command-palette-6): arrowing past the visible window scrolls the highlighted row into view (scrollTo anchor .center), so Return always activates a visible selection; guarded so empty results / index 0 don't crash.\n\nVISUAL: WP18 ships only two unused tokens (Theme.cornerRadius, SourceColors.longLabel) — ZERO user-visible change from WP18 alone. The visible effects (KPI corners 10→8, Settings showing \"iFlow\" not \"Iflow\") land when WP09/WP01/WP12 apply the tokens in their own files; those user-visible behaviors and their tests belong to those WPs.
- **Acceptance:**
  - Exactly one WP edits macos/Engram/Views/CommandPaletteView.swift in this batch (WP18). WP04 is re-scoped to SearchPageView.swift and any palette search-mode tweak is sequenced after WP18.
  - Command mode lists the navigation rows plus 3 action rows (Open Settings, Refresh Usage Data, Regenerate All Titles); Open Settings navigates to Settings; Refresh/Regenerate invoke the confirmed client method and dismiss.
  - No .action/.session PaletteCategory case is unreachable: action items use .action (actionCommands), session results use .session (sessionResult), navigation uses .navigation. The inline AnyPaletteRow struct is deleted.
  - MainWindowView no longer declares paletteItems or paletteSelection (grep returns zero matches); app still builds.
  - A selected session result row exposes Resume and Export affordances; Cmd-Return resumes (ResumeDialog sheet), Opt-Return exports via serviceClient.exportSession; plain Return still navigates.
  - Arrowing through a long result set keeps the selected row visible (ScrollViewReader.scrollTo on selectedIndex change).
  - Theme.cornerRadius == 8 exists (added, unused by WP18). SourceColors.longLabel(for:) exists and returns iFlow/Claude Code/Gemini CLI, falling back to label(for:) for unknown ids.
  - WP18's changed-files list equals exactly its 6 owned files: PaletteItem.swift, CommandPaletteView.swift, MainWindowView.swift, Theme.swift, SourceColors.swift, CommandPaletteTests.swift. WP18 edits NO file owned by WP09/WP01/WP15/WP12 and no unowned component file.
  - NO reindex/triggerSync wiring is added to the palette; no global Resume/Export action is added.
  - New CommandPaletteTests pass; existing ThemeTests/SourceColorsTests still pass.
- **Test plan:** Create macos/EngramTests/CommandPaletteTests.swift (@testable import Engram, XCTest), model-level, service-free:\n- testNavigationCommandsCoverAllScreens: PaletteItem.navigationCommands(navigate:{_ in}).count == Screen.allCases.count; every category == .navigation.\n- testActionCommandsAreThreeAndCategorized: actionCommands(navigate:refreshUsage:regenerateTitles:) returns 3 items, all category == .action, non-empty title+icon, empty secondaryActions; invoking each item.action sets a corresponding captured flag (verifies closure wiring).\n- testSessionResultIsSessionCategoryWithTwoSecondaryActions: PaletteItem.sessionResult(...) category == .session, primary action calls onSelect, secondaryActions.count == 2 with labels Resume/Export invoking onResume/onExport.\n- testLongLabelDisambiguatesAndFallsBack: SourceColors.longLabel(for:\"iflow\")==\"iFlow\"; (\"claude-code\")==\"Claude Code\"; (\"gemini-cli\")==\"Gemini CLI\"; (\"totally-unknown\")==SourceColors.label(for:\"totally-unknown\").\n- testThemeCornerRadiusTokenIsEight: XCTAssertEqual(Theme.cornerRadius, 8).\nRationale: pure/synchronous additions (model factories, label map, token) are fully unit-testable; async service calls are exercised only as closure wiring (captured-flag), keeping tests deterministic per the test-boundary convention. The xc-visual-4 BEHAVIOR change (Settings renders \"iFlow\" not \"Iflow\") is tested in WP12 (the SettingsView owner), NOT here — WP18 only owns the SourceColors.longLabel unit test. View-layer key-handling/sheet presentation is not unit-tested (SwiftUI interaction), consistent with existing palette/dialog views.
- **Risks:** onKeyPress modifiers: the closure overload .onKeyPress { keyPress in } exposing keyPress.modifiers is macOS 14.0 (confirmed deployment target), so it compiles; real Cmd-Return/Opt-Return delivery to a focused TextField should be smoke-checked on device — if the field swallows Return, the on-row Resume/Export buttons remain as a graceful fallback (command-palette-4 still closed by the visible affordances). ResumeDialog presented as a sheet over the palette sheet is sheet-over-sheet; if it misbehaves, fallback is to dismiss the palette then post .openSession (one extra hop, no crash). HANDOFF RISK: xc-visual-2/3/4 only fully CLOSE when the owning WPs apply the tokens — WP18 alone leaves the tokens unused. This is intentional and the disposition-disciplined outcome (WP18 cannot edit other WPs' files); the orchestrator must dispatch the paired call-site edits (WP09: KPICard radius+green/red; WP01: SessionCard/ExpandableSessionCard radius; WP15: AlertBanner orange; WP12: SettingsView longLabel repoint + Iflow→iFlow + test; a TierBar owner: TierBar hex→tokens). If those handoffs are not scheduled, the findings stay open and the WP18 tokens are dead until then — flagged explicitly so it is a conscious sequencing decision, not a silent miss. No service writes bypass EngramServiceClient.
- **Out of scope:** WP18 ships the PALETTE cluster + the TWO shared tokens ONLY. It deliberately does NOT:\n- Edit any file outside its 6 owned files. Per the critique, the call-site applications of cornerRadius/longLabel/the xc-visual-2 hex swaps live in WP09 (KPICard), WP01 (SessionCard/ExpandableSessionCard), WP15 (AlertBanner), WP12 (SettingsView), and a TierBar owner. Those are reassigned to the owning WPs; WP18 only provides the tokens.\n- Cover xc-visual-2 at all (its only call sites are in other WPs' files; the literals already equal the tokens so there is nothing to ADD here). Removed from findingsCovered; reassigned to WP09/WP15 + TierBar owner.\n- Do the SettingsView repoint or the \"Iflow\"→\"iFlow\" casing fix (SettingsView.swift is WP12's; SourceColors.label already has the correct casing, so WP12 just points displayName + defaultRows at SourceColors.longLabel and adds the Settings-renders-iFlow test).\n- Add a Re-index/Refresh-Index command (no reindex method; triggerSync is a confirmed stub) or any global Resume/Export \"current session\" action (the global palette has no current-session context — Resume/Export are scoped to session result rows where the id is in hand).\n- Touch xc-visual-1 (raw .secondary sites) or xc-visual-5 (raw status colors): the tokens those findings want already exist; the remaining work is a mechanical multi-file call-site sweep across files WP18 does not own — deferred to a dedicated sweep.\n- Add session Hide/Rename to the palette (owned by WPs targeting ExpandableSessionCard/SessionDetailView context menus).\nOWNERSHIP NOTE: WP18 now takes SOLE ownership of CommandPaletteView.swift; WP04 is re-scoped to SearchPageView.swift, with any palette search-mode tweak sequenced AFTER WP18.

## Added/amended after human decisions (2026-06-14)

### WP17 — AMENDED (Observability honesty: log-fix + Developer-Tools gating ONLY)

WP17 **no longer deletes** Performance/Traces (decision #2/#3 build real telemetry — see WP20). Revised WP17 scope:
- Fix the OSLog reader/redaction (un-redact both interpolation paths in `EngramLogger`/`ServiceLogger`) and remove the dead `warn` filter path.
- Document the Health tab's real signal and the inert `health()` stub.
- **Gate the whole Observability surface behind a default-off "Developer Tools" flag** at the `ObservabilityView` container level (so all 5 tabs, including WP20's Performance/Traces, are hidden from normal users).
- Repair the UITest target (ObservabilityTests + ObservabilityScreen + TestLaunchConfig) for the gate + reader change.
- **Drops** `PerformanceView.swift` + `TraceExplorerView.swift` from its owned files (WP20 owns them). WP17 ↔ WP20 interface only through the container gate, not shared files → can run in parallel once the gate API is agreed.

### WP19 — Cost dashboard (NEW, mixed: wire dead Settings controls + surface MCP-only cost data)

- **Closes:** usage-cost-1 (per-dollar spend never shown), usage-cost-2 (`dailyCostBudget`/`notifyOnCostThreshold` have no consumer).
- **Goal:** add a read-only `costs` service IPC command mirroring the MCP `getCosts` aggregate; render total spend + per-source breakdown + 30-day trend on Source Pulse; wire `dailyCostBudget`/`notifyOnCostThreshold` to a real budget-breach notification.
- **Approach:** `session_costs` is already populated (by `StartupUsageCollector`) and queried by `MCPDatabase.getCosts` (confirmed `macos/EngramMCP/Core/MCPDatabase.swift:196-251`) — but the app talks only to `EngramService`, not `MCPDatabase`. Add a parallel service read command following the `sources` pattern (protocol → client `command("costs")` → handler switch → `EngramServiceReadProvider.costs()` grouped query gated by `tableExists("session_costs")`). Render a display-only `CostSummarySection` on `SourcePulseView`. Add a **separate `CostBudgetNotifier`** (≈40 LOC, mirrors `UsagePressureNotifier`) driven off `MenuBarController`'s existing 10s `badgeTimer`, fetching today's spend via `costs()`, day-keyed dedup so it fires at most once/day; cleared when disabled/zero-budget.
- **Changes:** edit service cluster (EngramServiceProtocol/Client/Models/CommandHandler/ReadProvider/MockEngramServiceClient — append a `costs` command + DTOs `EngramServiceCostsResponse`/`…CostSourceRow`/`…CostDayRow`); create `macos/Engram/Views/Usage/CostSummarySection.swift`; edit `SourcePulseView.swift` (cost section only); create `macos/Engram/CostBudgetNotifier.swift`; edit `MenuBarController.swift` (notifier wiring only); create `EngramServiceCostsTests.swift` + `CostBudgetNotifierTests.swift`.
- **Schema (confirmed `EngramMigrations.swift:204-213`):** `session_costs(session_id PK, model, input_tokens, output_tokens, cache_read_tokens, cache_creation_tokens, cost_usd REAL, computed_at)`; source/day come from joined `sessions`. Per-source `SUM(cost_usd) GROUP BY s.source`; per-day `GROUP BY date(s.start_time)`; total rounded to cents; GUI adds `WHERE s.hidden_at IS NULL` (declared divergence from MCP for GUI consistency).
- **UX:** loading/empty("No cost data yet")/error(reuse `AlertBanner`, never blanks page); display-only; budget breach → one notification/local-day "Engram daily budget reached — $X of $Y".
- **Acceptance/tests:** `costs()` aggregates per-source+per-day, empty (not error) when table absent; budget notification fires once/day only when enabled & spend≥budget; existing 6 UsagePressure tests unaffected. Tests: `EngramServiceCostsTests` (seed sessions+session_costs, assert aggregate) + `CostBudgetNotifierTests` (breach/dedup/disabled/re-arm).
- **Wave:** serialized service-file cluster, AFTER WP06 DTO/IPC base. WP19-exclusive: CostSummarySection, SourcePulseView(cost), CostBudgetNotifier, MenuBarController(wiring), 2 tests.
- **Out of scope:** `monthlyCostBudget`/`notifyOnLongSession` stay unwired (separate gaps; flagged not deleted). Cost coverage is "spend Engram can compute," not billing-authoritative — empty/partial copy must not imply completeness.

### WP20 — Observability telemetry (NEW, backfill-data: real bounded Performance + Traces)

- **Closes:** observability-3, observability-4 (Performance/Traces permanent empty placeholders). Owns `PerformanceView.swift` + `TraceExplorerView.swift` (taken from WP17).
- **Goal:** real, **bounded, in-process** telemetry — no persistence, no new DB table, no external infra. Performance = rolling perf counters (last scan duration, indexed/total, scan count, per-command count/p50/p95/max/errors). Traces = last N (200) per-command spans (command, start, durationMs, ok/error) from an in-memory ring buffer.
- **Approach:** new `ServiceTelemetryCollector` **actor** (span ring buffer cap 200; per-command latency aggregates with bounded ~100-sample window; scan counters). Instrument the **single dispatch seam** `EngramServiceCommandHandler.handle(_:)` (confirmed `:37`) with monotonic `ContinuousClock` timing → record span; exclude `status` (poll noise) and `telemetry` (self). Instrument the scan body in `EngramServiceRunner` (reuse already-computed `scan.indexed`/`status.total` at `:342-350` + a stopwatch → `recordScan`). New read-only IPC `telemetry` command mirrors `health`'s shape but reads the collector (process state), not the SQLite read provider (justified deviation). Handler gains optional `telemetry:` ctor param defaulting `nil` so all existing constructors/tests compile unchanged.
- **Changes:** create `macos/EngramService/Core/ServiceTelemetryCollector.swift`; edit `EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift` (timing wrap + `case "telemetry"` + ctor param); edit `EngramServiceRunner.swift` (collector + scan timing); edit service cluster (Models/Protocol/Client/MockEngramServiceClient — add `ServiceTelemetrySnapshot`/`ServiceSpan`/`ServiceCommandLatency` + `telemetry()`); edit `PerformanceView.swift` + `TraceExplorerView.swift` (render, reuse `StatusBadge`/`KPICard`, 30s refresh off-main like `SystemHealthView`); create `ServiceTelemetryTests.swift`.
- **UX:** rendered inside WP17's gated Observability surface. Performance: KPI row + per-command latency table; "collected-but-empty" EmptyState before any command ("No performance data yet — run a search or wait for the next index scan"). Traces: newest-first span list with OK/ERROR badge + duration + relative time; empty copy "No spans recorded yet."
- **Acceptance/tests:** ring buffer caps at 200; per-command percentiles correct; failed command → span `ok=false`+errorName, latency errorCount≥1; `status`/`telemetry` not self-recorded; views load off-main; existing handler constructors/tests compile unchanged. Tests in `ServiceTelemetryTests` (ring eviction, percentiles, scan counters, span-on-dispatch, error-span, exclusion, IPC round-trip) modeled on `EngramServiceIPCTests:144-165`.
- **Wave:** serialized service-file cluster, AFTER WP06. WP20-exclusive: ServiceTelemetryCollector, PerformanceView, TraceExplorerView, ServiceTelemetryTests. **WP17 conflict resolved:** WP20 sole-owns the two views; WP17 drops them.
- **Out of scope (honest):** ephemeral (resets per service restart, no history/retention/time-series); NOT distributed tracing (flat per-command spans, no trace trees/IDs); coarse granularity (one span per IPC command; scan summarized as one duration not 4 phases); percentiles approximate (bounded window). Deliberate bounded trade — 90% of the "is it slow / what's erroring / how long was the last scan" value without a tracing stack.

> **Updated wave note:** WP19 + WP20 join the serialized service-file cluster {WP05, WP06, WP13, WP14, WP16} → now {WP05, WP06, WP13, WP14, WP16, WP19, WP20}. All edit `EngramServiceModels.swift` + others edit `EngramServiceReadProvider.swift`/`EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift`, so they serialize behind WP06's base. The non-service halves (views, notifiers, tests) parallelize freely. WP17 and WP20 run in parallel after the views-ownership split.

---

## Codex adversarial review corrections + REVISED execution model (2026-06-15)

Codex (gpt-5.5, xhigh, read-only) reviewed this design against the real source. Verdict: source-code assumptions mostly hold (WP01 closures, WP05 replay data exists in the adapter layer, WP06 save/delete backend exists, WP14 hideEmptySessions + hygiene stub location all confirmed), BUT the wave/closure/ordering had blockers. Resolutions applied:

**Blocker 1 — stale wave table → SERIAL service lane.** The 4-wave "parallel service WPs" model is WRONG now that {WP05,06,13,14,16,19,20} all edit the single-point seams `EngramServiceModels.swift` / `EngramServiceReadProvider.swift` / `EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift`. **Replaced by the two-stage model below.**

**Blocker 2 — WP13 reads `liveSyncDisabled` (owned by WP16) cross-wave → won't compile.** Resolution: the `EngramServiceSourceInfo.liveSyncDisabled` field moves into **Stage 0** (service base), so both WP13 and WP16 consume an already-existing field.

**Major 3 — WP20 finding IDs.** WP20 closes **observability-1** (Performance/Traces placeholders), NOT observability-3/-4. WP17 keeps observability-3 (redaction) + observability-4 (warn filter).

**Major 4 — WP19 usage-cost-2 partial.** Stage 0 wires **daily AND monthly** cost budget (both are simple aggregates); **long-session notify is DEFERRED** (needs live-session duration tracking). usage-cost-2 labeled PARTIAL with the long-session limb called out.

**Major 5 — WP13 sources-sync-3 partial.** Two Sources surfaces remain (SourcePulseView + SourcesSettingsSection); WP13 MITIGATES (honest badges + de-drift) but does not consolidate. Labeled **PARTIAL**.

**Major 6 — WP02 ↔ WP18 router conflict.** `Screen.favorites` forces edits to `Screen.swift` exhaustive switches + `MainWindowView.pageView`, which WP18 also owns. Resolution: a **single "navigation" agent owns `Screen.swift` + `MainWindowView.swift`** and lands BOTH WP02's favorites route and WP18's palette wiring; WP02/WP18's other files stay with them.

**Minor 7 — WP19 second notifier.** Extend the existing `UsagePressureNotifier` (shared timer/dedupe/settings seam) instead of a new `CostBudgetNotifier`.

**Minor 8 — WP20 scan instrumentation.** Instrument BOTH the initial startup scan and the periodic scan in `EngramServiceRunner` (not just periodic).

### REVISED EXECUTION MODEL

**Stage 0 — Service base (SERIAL, single working tree, build-gated).** One coordinated additive pass implementing every shared-seam service change so the cluster never merge-conflicts:
- `EngramServiceModels.swift`: `EngramServiceMemoryFile.content`; `EngramServiceSourceInfo.liveSyncDisabled`; insights + costs + telemetry DTOs.
- `EngramServiceProtocol.swift` / `EngramServiceClient.swift` / `MockEngramServiceClient.swift`: `insights()`, `costs()`, `telemetry()`.
- `EngramServiceReadProvider.swift`: `insights()`, `costs()` (per-source + per-day + month-to-date), `liveSyncDisabled` in `sources()`, replay backfill (WP05 — role/timestamp/tool/token from adapter stream).
- `EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift`: cases `insights`/`costs`/`telemetry`; real hygiene checks (WP14); telemetry span instrumentation + optional `telemetry:` ctor param (default nil).
- `EngramServiceRunner.swift`: telemetry collector wiring + initial AND periodic scan timing.
- New: `ServiceTelemetryCollector.swift`, `LiveSyncDisabledSources.swift`.
- **GATE:** `xcodegen generate` + build EngramService + run EngramServiceCoreTests; do not proceed until green.

**Stage 0.5 — Shared tokens + navigation (SERIAL, small).** `Theme.cornerRadius` + `SourceColors.longLabel` (WP18 tokens, before consumers). The single navigation agent lands `Screen.favorites` + `MainWindowView` router for both WP02 and WP18.

**Stage 1 — UI (PARALLEL, file-disjoint, shared tree, build-gated).** All UI WPs run concurrently, each owning distinct view files, consuming the Stage-0 client methods: WP01, WP03, WP04, WP05-views, WP06-views, WP07, WP08, WP09, WP10, WP11, WP12, WP13-views, WP14-view, WP15, WP16-views, WP17, WP19-view+notifier, WP20-views. Build gate + tests after the wave; conflicts impossible by construction (service seam already frozen, navigation already done, each agent's files disjoint).
